The Second Zahiri Argument and Its Refutation
Second Zahiri argument and its refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second Zahiri argument based on perfect knowledge and its refutation, including the obligation according to capacity and the role of Shari'ah.

Core Idea
Our obligation is according to capacity, not absolute knowledge.

The Zahiris also argued that if additional attributes existed, the perfect knowers would know them. This lesson unpacks that argument and shows how the author refutes it by limiting obligation and pointing to Shari'ah as a source of knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note that this argument has two parts: the perfect knowers' knowledge and the limited ways to know attributes.
The refutation is detailed: denying the obligation, questioning the knowledge of perfect knowers, and rejecting the limited means.
2
Analyze the Zahiri reasoning
The Zahiris claim we must know all attributes, yet we (perfect knowers) do not know additional ones, so they don't exist. Also, attributes can only be known through actions and transcendence, which don't indicate more.
3
Examine the refutation points
The author refutes by denying the obligation (we are only obligated according to capacity), questioning the assumption that perfect knowers didn't know another attribute, and rejecting the claim that Shari'ah is not a way to know attributes.
The final rhetorical question emphasizes Shari'ah as a valid source.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث السابع : في صفات اختلف فيها يعني اختلف فيها أهل الحق القائلون بالصفات الأزلية . زعم بعض الظاهرية أنه لا صفة الله تعالى وراء السبعة المذكورة لوجهين : أحدهما : أنه لا دليل عليه وكل ما لا دليل عليه يجب نفيه، ورد بمنع المقدمتين. وثانيهما: أنا مكلفون بكمال المعرفة، وذلك بمعرفة الذات وجميع الصفات فلم كانت له صفات أخرى لعرفناها معشر العارفين الكاملين واللازم منتف بالضرورة وبأنه لا طريق إلى معرفة الصفات سوى الاستدلال بالأفعال، والتنزيه عن النقائص، وهما لا يدلان على صفة أخرى، ورد بالمنع بل التكليف بقدر الوسع . ولو سلم فما أدريك أن الكاملين لم يعرفوا صفة أخرى ، ولا نسلم أنه لا طريق سوى ما ذكرتم . أليس الشرع طريقاً قويماً، وصراطاً مستقياً ؟
The seventh investigation: concerning attributes that are disputed, meaning the people of truth who affirm the eternal attributes disagreed among themselves. Some of the Zahiris claimed that there is no attribute of Allah Almighty beyond the seven mentioned, based on two aspects: First: there is no evidence for it, and everything for which there is no evidence must be denied—refuted by denying both premises. Second: we are obligated to perfect knowledge, and that is by knowing the essence and all attributes; so if He had other attributes, we, the community of perfect knowers, would know them, and the consequent is necessarily negated—and because there is no way to know attributes except by inference from actions and transcendence of imperfections, and both do not indicate another attribute—refuted by denying it, rather the obligation is according to capacity. And if it were granted, what makes you think that the perfect knowers did not know another attribute? And we do not concede that there is no way other than what you mentioned. Is not the Shari'ah a straight path and a direct way?
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Zahiri position that God has no attributes beyond the seven well-known ones. The author first states the Zahiri claim and their two proofs: (1) no proof exists for additional attributes, and whatever has no proof must be denied, and (2) we are obligated to perfect knowledge, which requires knowing the essence and all attributes; if there were others, the perfect knowers would know them. The author refutes both: first, by denying the premises (the claim that there is no proof and the claim that lack of proof necessitates denial). Second, by denying that the obligation is to know all attributes – rather, obligation is according to capacity. Furthermore, he questions: 'What makes you think the perfect knowers did not know another attribute?' And he denies that there is no way to know attributes except through actions and transcendence; rather, the Shari'ah is a straight path and a direct way.

Key Terms
التكليف بقدر الوسع
العارفين الكاملين
الشرع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: We must know everything about Allah to fulfill our obligation.
Correction: Our obligation is according to our capacity; we are not required to know all attributes exhaustively. Also, Shari'ah provides knowledge of attributes beyond what reason alone can deduce.

Checkpoint
How does the author refute the claim that we are obligated to perfect knowledge of all attributes?
A) By asserting that we are not obligated to know any attributes.
B) By saying obligation is according to capacity, not absolute.
C) By arguing that perfect knowers do exist and know all.
D) By denying that attributes can be known at all.

Key Takeaway
The second Zahiri argument fails because our duty is limited by capacity, we cannot assume perfect knowers know everything, and Shari'ah provides additional ways to know attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about your own knowledge of God, do you ever assume you have 'perfect' understanding? Where in your life do you need to admit that your capacity is limited and that your obligation is only to seek what you can bear? What would change if you truly accepted that?
?
The Zahiris claimed that if God had other attributes, the perfect knowers would know them. Have you ever dismissed a truth about God because it wasn't obvious to you or to the people you consider elite? What if God has revealed things in the Shari'ah that your reason alone cannot reach—will you submit to that revelation today?
?
This lesson says the Shari'ah is 'a straight path and a direct way' to know God. Are you actually using the Shari'ah—the Quran and Sunnah—as your primary source for knowing His attributes, or do you rely more on your own reasoning and what 'makes sense' to you? What step will you take this week to learn one attribute of God directly from revelation?

Al-Baqa': The Ash'ari Proof and the Majority's Objections
Ash'ari asserts baqa' as an attribute and the majority counter with two objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari argument for baqa' as an additional attribute and the two main objections from the majority that baqa' is not additional to existence.

Core Idea
The existence of a thing does not guarantee its permanence; thus the Necessary Being must have baqa' as a distinct attribute.

The attribute of al-baqa' (permanence) is one of the disputed divine attributes. Ash'aris affirm it as a meaning subsisting in the divine essence, distinct from existence itself. In this passage, al-Ash'ari presents his proof and then the majority raise two objections, arguing that baqa' is merely existence continued in time. We will unpack each part.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the overall flow. Notice the shift from Ash'ari's proof to the majority's objections.
2
Identify the proof and the objections
Ash'ari's proof: because the Necessary is permanent, there must be a meaning of permanence. Then two objections: first, baqa' is just existence related to a second time; second, if baqa' were additional, it would compromise self-sufficiency.
3
Reflect on the dialectic
Notice how each side uses the concept of necessity. The majority's second objection is especially sharp: an added attribute would make the Necessary dependent.
This connects to the broader debate on divine simplicity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فمن الصفات المختلف فيها البقاء أثبته الشيخ الأشعري وأشياعه من أهل السنة . لأن الواجب باق بالضرورة، فلا بد أن يقوم به معنى هو البقاء كما في العالم والقادر ، لأن البقاء ليس من السلوب والإضافات وهو ظاهر، وليس أيضاً عبارة عن الوجود، بل زائداً عليه لأن الشيء قد يوجد ولا يبقى كالأعراض ، سيما السيالة، وذهب الأكثرون إلى أنه ليس صفة زائدة على الوجود لوجوه : . أحدها: أن المعقول منه استمرار الوجود ولا معنى لذلك سوى الوجود من حيث انتسابه إلى الزمان الثاني بعد الزمان الأول وثانيها : أن الواجب لو كان باقياً بالبقاء الذي ليس نفس ذاته، لما كان واجب الوجود لذاته، لأن ما هو موجود لذاته، لذاته، فهو باق لذاته ضرورة أن ما بالذات لا يزول أبداً، وإذا فسر البقاء بصيغة بها الوجود في الزمان الثاني كان لزوم المحال أظهر لأنه يؤول إلى أن الواجب موجود في الزمان الثاني لأمر سوى ذاته . واعترض صاحب الصحائف بأن اللازم ليس إلا افتقار صفة إلى صفة أخرى نشأت من الذات ولا امتناع فيه كالإرادة تتوقف على العلم والعلم على الحياة، وليس بشيء لأن الوجود ليس من الذات . ولو سلم فافتقاره إلى أمر سوى الذات ينافي الوجوب بالذات .
Among the disputed attributes is al-baqa' (permanence). Shaykh al-Ash'ari and his followers among the Ahl al-Sunnah affirm it, because the Necessary Being is necessarily baqin (permanent), so there must subsist in Him a meaning which is baqa', just as in the knowing and the powerful. For al-baqa' is not among negations or relations, and that is apparent; nor is it an expression for existence, but rather additional to it, because a thing may exist and not remain (yabqa), like accidents, especially the transitory ones. The majority went to the view that it is not an attribute additional to existence, for reasons: First: that what is understood from it is the continuation of existence (istimrar al-wujud), and there is no meaning to that other than existence in terms of its relation to the second time after the first time. Second: that if the Necessary were baqin by a baqa' that is not identical to His essence, He would not be necessary of existence in essence, because that which exists by essence, by itself, is baqin by essence necessarily, for that which is by essence never ceases. And if baqa' is interpreted as existence in the second time, the implication of absurdity is more evident, because it leads to the Necessary being existent in the second time due to something other than His essence. And Sahib al-Saha'if objected that the necessary consequence is only the dependence of an attribute on another attribute arising from the essence, and there is no impossibility in that, like will depending on knowledge and knowledge on life. But it is nothing, because existence is not from the essence. And even if granted, its dependence on something other than the essence contradicts necessity by essence.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage begins the discussion of the attribute al-baqa' (permanence). The author states that Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and his followers affirm baqa' as an attribute because the Necessary Being is necessarily baqin (permanent), so there must subsist in Him a meaning (ma'na) that is baqa', just as in the case of knowledge and power. This is because baqa' is not a negation (salb) or relation (idafa), nor is it identical to existence, since things may exist but not continue, like accidents, especially transitory ones. The majority, however, argue that baqa' is not additional to existence. They give two reasons. First: baqa' rationally means continuation of existence, which is just existence itself considered in relation to a second time. Second: if the Necessary were baqin by a baqa' not identical to His essence, then He would not be necessary in essence, because that which exists by essence is baqin by essence. If baqa' is interpreted as existence in a second time, then the Necessary would exist in the second time due to something other than His essence, which contradicts necessity. The author then reports an objection from Sahib al-Saha'if (al-Samarqandi): the only consequence is that an attribute depends on another attribute arising from the essence, which is not impossible, like will depending on knowledge and knowledge on life. The author disagrees: existence is not from the essence. Even if granted, dependence on something other than the essence contradicts necessity by essence.

Key Terms
البقاء
الواجب
الوجود
الزمان الثاني
السلب والإضافة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Baqa' is simply a synonym for existence and adds no new meaning.
Correction: The passage shows that things can exist without persisting (e.g., accidents), so baqa' must be a distinct meaning from existence.

Checkpoint
According to the majority's first objection, what does baqa' mean?
A) A new attribute subsisting in the essence
B) Continuation of existence, which is existence related to a second time
C) Negation of non-existence
D) A relation to the essence

Key Takeaway
The Ash'aris argue for baqa' as an additional attribute because existence alone does not entail permanence, while the majority counter that baqa' is merely existence continued in time, and an additional attribute would undermine divine self-sufficiency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe in God's absolute permanence, or do you sometimes let fear and doubt cloud your trust that He is the same yesterday, today, and forever? What area of your life reveals that lack of trust, and what will you do to anchor yourself in His unchanging nature this week?
?
The majority warns that an additional attribute of permanence would imply God relies on something other than His essence. Examine your heart: are there people, possessions, or circumstances you treat as if they are necessary for your well-being, subtly denying God's self-sufficiency and your dependence on Him alone?
?
If baqa' is merely existence continued in time, then your very existence is a gift renewed every moment. How does that awareness change the way you will live the next hour — not just your thoughts, but your actions and words?

Responding to Sahib al-Saha'if's Objection on Baqa'
Sahib al-Saha'if objects, and the author offers a two-part rebuttal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection by Sahib al-Saha'if against the majority's second argument and the author's rebuttal that dependence on something other than essence contradicts necessity.

Core Idea
Dependence on another attribute arising from the essence is not the same as dependence on something outside the essence.

After presenting the majority's two objections, the author reports an objection by Sahib al-Saha'if (al-Samarqandi) who tries to defend the majority by arguing that the dependence of an attribute on another attribute is permissible, like will depending on knowledge. The author rejects this, asserting that existence is not from the essence and that even if it were, such dependence violates necessity by essence. We will examine this exchange closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Understand Sahib al-Saha'if's argument: the only consequence is attribute dependence on another attribute, which is not impossible. He gives an example from will and knowledge.
2
Examine the author's rebuttal
The author gives two reasons: first, existence is not from the essence; second, even if it were, dependence on something other than the essence contradicts necessity by essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فمن الصفات المختلف فيها البقاء أثبته الشيخ الأشعري وأشياعه من أهل السنة . لأن الواجب باق بالضرورة، فلا بد أن يقوم به معنى هو البقاء كما في العالم والقادر ، لأن البقاء ليس من السلوب والإضافات وهو ظاهر، وليس أيضاً عبارة عن الوجود، بل زائداً عليه لأن الشيء قد يوجد ولا يبقى كالأعراض ، سيما السيالة، وذهب الأكثرون إلى أنه ليس صفة زائدة على الوجود لوجوه : . أحدها: أن المعقول منه استمرار الوجود ولا معنى لذلك سوى الوجود من حيث انتسابه إلى الزمان الثاني بعد الزمان الأول وثانيها : أن الواجب لو كان باقياً بالبقاء الذي ليس نفس ذاته، لما كان واجب الوجود لذاته، لأن ما هو موجود لذاته، لذاته، فهو باق لذاته ضرورة أن ما بالذات لا يزول أبداً، وإذا فسر البقاء بصيغة بها الوجود في الزمان الثاني كان لزوم المحال أظهر لأنه يؤول إلى أن الواجب موجود في الزمان الثاني لأمر سوى ذاته . واعترض صاحب الصحائف بأن اللازم ليس إلا افتقار صفة إلى صفة أخرى نشأت من الذات ولا امتناع فيه كالإرادة تتوقف على العلم والعلم على الحياة، وليس بشيء لأن الوجود ليس من الذات . ولو سلم فافتقاره إلى أمر سوى الذات ينافي الوجوب بالذات .
Among the disputed attributes is al-baqa' (permanence). Shaykh al-Ash'ari and his followers among the Ahl al-Sunnah affirm it, because the Necessary Being is necessarily baqin (permanent), so there must subsist in Him a meaning which is baqa', just as in the knowing and the powerful. For al-baqa' is not among negations or relations, and that is apparent; nor is it an expression for existence, but rather additional to it, because a thing may exist and not remain (yabqa), like accidents, especially the transitory ones. The majority went to the view that it is not an attribute additional to existence, for reasons: First: that what is understood from it is the continuation of existence (istimrar al-wujud), and there is no meaning to that other than existence in terms of its relation to the second time after the first time. Second: that if the Necessary were baqin by a baqa' that is not identical to His essence, He would not be necessary of existence in essence, because that which exists by essence, by itself, is baqin by essence necessarily, for that which is by essence never ceases. And if baqa' is interpreted as existence in the second time, the implication of absurdity is more evident, because it leads to the Necessary being existent in the second time due to something other than His essence. And Sahib al-Saha'if objected that the necessary consequence is only the dependence of an attribute on another attribute arising from the essence, and there is no impossibility in that, like will depending on knowledge and knowledge on life. But it is nothing, because existence is not from the essence. And even if granted, its dependence on something other than the essence contradicts necessity by essence.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage begins the discussion of the attribute al-baqa' (permanence). The author states that Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and his followers affirm baqa' as an attribute because the Necessary Being is necessarily baqin (permanent), so there must subsist in Him a meaning (ma'na) that is baqa', just as in the case of knowledge and power. This is because baqa' is not a negation (salb) or relation (idafa), nor is it identical to existence, since things may exist but not continue, like accidents, especially transitory ones. The majority, however, argue that baqa' is not additional to existence. They give two reasons. First: baqa' rationally means continuation of existence, which is just existence itself considered in relation to a second time. Second: if the Necessary were baqin by a baqa' not identical to His essence, then He would not be necessary in essence, because that which exists by essence is baqin by essence. If baqa' is interpreted as existence in a second time, then the Necessary would exist in the second time due to something other than His essence, which contradicts necessity. The author then reports an objection from Sahib al-Saha'if (al-Samarqandi): the only consequence is that an attribute depends on another attribute arising from the essence, which is not impossible, like will depending on knowledge and knowledge on life. The author disagrees: existence is not from the essence. Even if granted, dependence on something other than the essence contradicts necessity by essence.

Key Terms
صاحب الصحائف
الذات
الوجوب بالذات
الإرادة
العلم
الحياة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All dependence in God is equally impossible.
Correction: Dependence of one attribute on another that both arise from the essence is permissible (e.g., will depends on knowledge). What is impossible is dependence on something outside the essence.

Checkpoint
What did Sahib al-Saha'if use as an example to show permissible attribute dependence?
A) Will depending on knowledge
B) Knowledge depending on life
C) Both A and B
D) Power depending on will

Key Takeaway
The author argues that an additional baqa' attribute would make the Necessary dependent on something outside His essence, which violates the very meaning of necessary existence by essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever treat God's attributes as if they were independent add-ons, rather than seeing His essence as the source? How does that affect your understanding of His oneness?
?
When you rely on something other than God's essence, like your own knowledge or will, do you realize that this contradicts the very meaning of His necessity? How can you realign your trust?
?
The author insists that dependency on something outside the essence negates necessary existence. In what areas of your life are you making God dependent on your actions? How can you affirm His absolute independence?

Third Argument: The Trilemma Against Baqa'
Sanusi presents the third argument as a trilemma against baqa' as an additional attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the trilemma (dawr, khulf, ta'addud al-wajib) presented as the third argument against baqa' as an additional attribute, and why each horn is problematic.

Core Idea
The third argument traps the doctrine of baqa' in a trilemma: circularity, contradiction, or multiple necessary beings.

The majority theologians argue that if baqa' were an additional attribute, it would lead to one of three absurdities. This trilemma is a powerful logical tool to show that the divine essence must be eternal by itself. In this lesson, we will trace the reasoning behind each horn and see why the Ash'ari position fails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the trilemma structure
Recognize that the argument presents three possibilities for dependence between the essence and baqa'.
Each horn is spelled out clearly in the passage.
2
First horn: circularity (dawr)
If baqa' depends on the essence, then each needs the other for continuance in the second time, leading to circularity.
Circularity is invalid because it prevents independent subsistence.
3
Second horn: contradiction (khulf)
If the essence depends on baqa', then baqa' would be the necessary being, not the essence—a contradiction.
This contradicts the primacy of the divine essence.
4
Third horn: multiplicity of the necessary (ta'addud al-wajib)
If neither depends on the other, each would be independent of everything, implying multiple necessary existents.
This is impossible because only one necessary being exists.
5
Conclusion of the argument
All three horns are absurd, so the assumption that baqa' is an additional attribute must be false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وثالثها: أن الذات لو كان باقياً بالبقاء لا بنفسه، فإن افتقر صفة البقاء إلى الذات لزم الدور لتوقف ثبوت كل ما في الزمان الثاني على الآخر، وإن افتقر الذات إلى البقاء مع استغنائه عنه كان الواجب هو البقاء لا الذات هذا خلف، وإن لم يفتقر أحدهما على الآخر، بل اتفق تحققهما معاً كما ذكره صاحب المواقف لزم تعدد الواجب لأن كلا من الذات والبقاء يكون مستغنياً عما سواه، إذ لو افتقر البقاء إلى شيء لافتقر إلى الذات ضرورة افتقار الكل إليه والمستغني عن جميع ما سواه واجب قطعاً مع أن ما فرض من عدم افتقار البقاء إلى الذات محال، لأن افتقار الصفة إلى الذات ضروري. ورابعها أن البقاء لو كانت صفة أزلية زائدة على الذات قائمة به كانت باقية بالضرورة، وحينئذ فإن كان لها بقاء ينقل الكلام إليه بتسلسل وأيضاً يلزم قيام المعنى بالمعنى وهو باطل عندكم ، وإن لم يكن لها بقاء كان كعالم بلا علم وقد بين بطلانه . فإن قيل : هو باق بالبقاء إلا أن بقاءه نفسه لا زائداً عليه ليتسلسل قلنا : فحينئذ يجوز أن يكون الباري تعالى باقياً ببقاء هو نفسه عالماً بعلم هو نفسه، فلا يثبت زيادة
And their third: that if the essence were baqin (permanent) by baqa' not by itself, then either the attribute of baqa' depends on the essence – then circularity follows, because the subsistence of each in the second time depends on the other; or the essence depends on baqa' despite being independent of it – then the necessary would be the baqa', not the essence, which is a contradiction; or neither depends on the other, but rather they occur together as mentioned by Sahib al-Mawaqif – then the multiplicity of the necessary would follow, because each of the essence and baqa' would be independent of everything else, since if baqa' depended on anything, it would depend on the essence necessarily because everything depends on it, and that which is independent of everything else is necessarily necessary, although the assumption of baqa' not depending on the essence is impossible, because the dependence of an attribute on the essence is necessary. And their fourth: that if baqa' were an eternal attribute additional to the essence subsisting in Him, it would itself be necessarily baqin (permanent). Then if it had a baqa', the discussion would be passed on to it ad infinitum, and also it would entail the subsistence of a meaning in a meaning, which is invalid according to you. And if it did not have a baqa', it would be like a knower without knowledge, and its falsity has been shown. If it is said: it is baqin by baqa' except that its baqa' is itself, not additional to it, to avoid infinite regress, we say: then it would be permissible for the Exalted Creator to be baqin by a baqa' that is His essence, and knowing by knowledge that is His essence, so no additional attribute is established.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage presents the third and fourth arguments of the majority against baqa' as an additional attribute. The third argument is a trilemma: if the essence were baqin by a baqa' not by itself, then either (a) the attribute baqa' depends on the essence – leading to circularity (dawr) because each depends on the other for continuance in a second time; (b) the essence depends on baqa' despite being self-sufficient – then baqa' would be the necessary, not the essence (khulf); (c) neither depends on the other, but both occur together as al-Mawaqif suggests – then both would be independent of everything else, leading to multiple necessary existents (ta'addud al-wajib). Moreover, baqa' cannot be independent of the essence because attributes necessarily depend on the essence. The fourth argument: if baqa' were an eternal attribute additional to the essence, then baqa' itself would be baqin necessarily, requiring either another baqa' ad infinitum (tasalsul) – invalid, and also implying subsistence of meaning in meaning – which is invalid; or baqa' would not be baqin – then it would be like a knower without knowledge, which is false. An objector says: baqa' is baqin by itself without additional baqa'. The author replies: then by analogy, God could be baqin by a baqa' that is His essence and knowing by knowledge that is His essence, thus no additional attributes are established.

Key Terms
الدور
الخلف
تعدد الواجب
صاحب المواقف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The third argument is simply about circularity.
Correction: The argument actually presents three distinct horns: circularity, contradiction, and multiplicity of the necessary. Each must be refuted independently.

Checkpoint
According to the third argument, what follows if the essence and baqa' are assumed to be independent of each other and occur together?
A) Circularity.
B) Infinite regress.
C) The multiplicity of the necessary (ta'addud al-wajib).
D) A contradiction (khulf).

Key Takeaway
The trilemma shows that the assumption of baqa' as an additional attribute leads to either circularity, contradiction, or multiple necessary beings, all of which are impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about God's attributes, do you ever treat them as separate 'things' that God 'has' rather than aspects of His very essence? How does this trilemma expose the incoherence of such a mindset?
?
This argument shows that any attempt to make God's attributes independent leads to absurdity. Is there an area of your faith where you subtly assume God's qualities are independent of His being? How will you correct that today?
?
The third horn leads to multiple necessary beings, which contradicts Tawhid. In your daily life, do you ever act as though there are 'little gods'—things you rely on as if they were independent of Allah? What must change?

Fourth Argument: Infinite Regress and the Objection
Sanusi presents the fourth argument with two options and answers the objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth argument against baqa' as an additional attribute, which leads to an infinite regress or the invalidity of a meaning subsisting in a meaning, and how the objection that baqa' is baqin by itself undermines the doctrine of additional attributes.

Core Idea
The fourth argument forces a choice between infinite regress and the impossibility of a meaning subsisting in a meaning.

The fourth argument shifts focus to the attribute itself: if baqa' is an eternal attribute, it must be eternal (baqin) itself. This leads to either an infinite regress (tasalsul) or the problematic notion of a meaning subsisting in a meaning. In this lesson, we'll examine the logic and the objection that baqa' is eternal by itself, and see how the rebuttal shows this undermines the doctrine of additional attributes.

Guided Path
1
Understand the premise of the fourth argument
If baqa' is an eternal attribute, it must itself be baqin (eternal). The question is whether it requires its own baqa'.
This is a crucial step to frame the dilemma.
2
First option: baqa' has its own baqa'
If it does, then an infinite regress follows, and also a meaning (baqa') subsists in another meaning (baqa'), which is invalid according to the opponents.
Infinite regress is unacceptable; meaning-in-meaning is also rejected.
3
Second option: baqa' does not have its own baqa'
If it lacks a baqa', then it would be like a knower without knowledge—a contradiction, as an eternal attribute must be eternal by nature.
This option is also false.
4
Consider the objection
An objector says baqa' is baqin by itself, not by an additional attribute, avoiding regress.
The objection seems plausible.
5
Analyze the rebuttal
If baqa' is baqin by itself, then the essence could be baqin by a baqa' that is its essence, and similarly knowing by knowledge that is its essence, making additional attributes unnecessary.
This rebuttal turns the objection on its head.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وثالثها: أن الذات لو كان باقياً بالبقاء لا بنفسه، فإن افتقر صفة البقاء إلى الذات لزم الدور لتوقف ثبوت كل ما في الزمان الثاني على الآخر، وإن افتقر الذات إلى البقاء مع استغنائه عنه كان الواجب هو البقاء لا الذات هذا خلف، وإن لم يفتقر أحدهما على الآخر، بل اتفق تحققهما معاً كما ذكره صاحب المواقف لزم تعدد الواجب لأن كلا من الذات والبقاء يكون مستغنياً عما سواه، إذ لو افتقر البقاء إلى شيء لافتقر إلى الذات ضرورة افتقار الكل إليه والمستغني عن جميع ما سواه واجب قطعاً مع أن ما فرض من عدم افتقار البقاء إلى الذات محال، لأن افتقار الصفة إلى الذات ضروري. ورابعها أن البقاء لو كانت صفة أزلية زائدة على الذات قائمة به كانت باقية بالضرورة، وحينئذ فإن كان لها بقاء ينقل الكلام إليه بتسلسل وأيضاً يلزم قيام المعنى بالمعنى وهو باطل عندكم ، وإن لم يكن لها بقاء كان كعالم بلا علم وقد بين بطلانه . فإن قيل : هو باق بالبقاء إلا أن بقاءه نفسه لا زائداً عليه ليتسلسل قلنا : فحينئذ يجوز أن يكون الباري تعالى باقياً ببقاء هو نفسه عالماً بعلم هو نفسه، فلا يثبت زيادة
And their third: that if the essence were baqin (permanent) by baqa' not by itself, then either the attribute of baqa' depends on the essence – then circularity follows, because the subsistence of each in the second time depends on the other; or the essence depends on baqa' despite being independent of it – then the necessary would be the baqa', not the essence, which is a contradiction; or neither depends on the other, but rather they occur together as mentioned by Sahib al-Mawaqif – then the multiplicity of the necessary would follow, because each of the essence and baqa' would be independent of everything else, since if baqa' depended on anything, it would depend on the essence necessarily because everything depends on it, and that which is independent of everything else is necessarily necessary, although the assumption of baqa' not depending on the essence is impossible, because the dependence of an attribute on the essence is necessary. And their fourth: that if baqa' were an eternal attribute additional to the essence subsisting in Him, it would itself be necessarily baqin (permanent). Then if it had a baqa', the discussion would be passed on to it ad infinitum, and also it would entail the subsistence of a meaning in a meaning, which is invalid according to you. And if it did not have a baqa', it would be like a knower without knowledge, and its falsity has been shown. If it is said: it is baqin by baqa' except that its baqa' is itself, not additional to it, to avoid infinite regress, we say: then it would be permissible for the Exalted Creator to be baqin by a baqa' that is His essence, and knowing by knowledge that is His essence, so no additional attribute is established.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage presents the third and fourth arguments of the majority against baqa' as an additional attribute. The third argument is a trilemma: if the essence were baqin by a baqa' not by itself, then either (a) the attribute baqa' depends on the essence – leading to circularity (dawr) because each depends on the other for continuance in a second time; (b) the essence depends on baqa' despite being self-sufficient – then baqa' would be the necessary, not the essence (khulf); (c) neither depends on the other, but both occur together as al-Mawaqif suggests – then both would be independent of everything else, leading to multiple necessary existents (ta'addud al-wajib). Moreover, baqa' cannot be independent of the essence because attributes necessarily depend on the essence. The fourth argument: if baqa' were an eternal attribute additional to the essence, then baqa' itself would be baqin necessarily, requiring either another baqa' ad infinitum (tasalsul) – invalid, and also implying subsistence of meaning in meaning – which is invalid; or baqa' would not be baqin – then it would be like a knower without knowledge, which is false. An objector says: baqa' is baqin by itself without additional baqa'. The author replies: then by analogy, God could be baqin by a baqa' that is His essence and knowing by knowledge that is His essence, thus no additional attributes are established.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection that baqa' is baqin by itself successfully defends the doctrine.
Correction: The objection fails because it would allow all attributes to be identical to the essence, eliminating the need for additional attributes.

Checkpoint
According to the fourth argument, what is one consequence if baqa' had its own baqa'?
A) Circularity.
B) Multiplicity of the necessary.
C) Infinite regress and meaning-in-meaning.
D) The attribute would be like a knower without knowledge.

Key Takeaway
The fourth argument shows that baqa' as an additional attribute leads to either infinite regress or a contradiction, and the objection that baqa' is self-subsisting is refuted because it would allow all attributes to be identical to the essence.

?
If the objection that baqa' is self-subsisting were true, it would collapse the distinction between God's essence and attributes. Are you willing to accept a conception of God where His attributes are identical to His essence, even if it challenges what you've been taught?
?
This argument demands that we think rigorously about God's nature. Do you truly seek to understand God through such logical reasoning, or do you prefer to avoid these deep questions? What does your answer reveal about your commitment to knowing God?

The Argument that Baqa' is by Essence
Sanusi argues for baqa' by essence and refutes an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument that Allah's endurance (baqa') is by His essence rather than an additional attribute, and how al-Sanusi responds to an objection from al-Sahā'if.

Core Idea
Allah's endurance is essential to His being, not an added quality.

This passage presents a key dialectical exchange in the debate over divine attributes. Al-Sanusi argues that for the Necessary Being, endurance must be by essence, not by an additional attribute, and then addresses a subtle objection from the author of al-Sahā'if. The argument hinges on the principle that what is essential never ceases.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: a claim, an objection, and a rebuttal.
2
Identify the main claim about baqa'
The argument begins by stating that what exists by itself is enduring by itself. Find this and understand why baqa' is said to be by essence.
The phrase 'ما بالذات لا يزول أبداً' (what is by essence never ceases) is key.
3
Understand the objection from al-Sahā'if
The objector argues that dependence of one attribute on another is permissible, using examples like will depending on knowledge. Locate this objection and grasp its point.
The objection is about attribute interdependence, not existence.
4
See how Sanusi refutes the objection
The refutation states that existence is not from the essence in the way attributes are, and if it were dependent, it would contradict necessity by essence.
The key line: 'الوجود ليس من الذات' (existence is not from the essence).
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this distinction matters for the doctrine of divine attributes and the concept of Necessary Being.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الذي ليس نفس ذاته، لما كان واجب الوجود لذاته، لأن ما هو موجود لذاته، لذاته، فهو باق لذاته ضرورة أن ما بالذات لا يزول أبداً، وإذا فسر البقاء بصيغة بها الوجود في الزمان الثاني كان لزوم المحال أظهر لأنه يؤول إلى أن الواجب موجود في الزمان الثاني لأمر سوى ذاته. واعترض صاحب الصحائف بأن اللازم ليس إلا افتقار صفة إلى صفة أخرى نشأت من الذات ولا امتناع فيه كالإرادة تتوقف على العلم والعلم على الحياة، وليس بشيء لأن الوجود ليس من الذات . ولو سلم فافتقاره إلى أمر سوى الذات ينافي الوجوب بالذات.
Which is not the essence itself, since the Necessary of Existence is necessary by itself, because what exists by itself, by itself, is enduring by itself necessarily, because that which is by essence never ceases; and if baqa' is interpreted as existence in the second time, the necessary impossibility becomes more apparent, because it leads to the Necessary being existing in the second time due to something other than itself. And the author of al-Sahā'if objected that the necessary consequence is only the dependence of one attribute on another attribute arising from the essence, and there is no impossibility in that, like will depending on knowledge and knowledge on life; and it is nothing because existence is not from the essence. And if it is granted, then its dependence on something other than the essence contradicts necessity by essence.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage presents an argument that the Necessary Being's baqa' (endurance) is by its own essence, not by an additional attribute. It begins by stating that what exists by itself is enduring by itself, and that what is essential never ceases. Then it raises a problem: if baqa' is defined as existence in a second time, then the Necessary Being would exist in that second time due to something other than its essence, which is impossible for a Necessary Being. The author of al-Sahā'if objects that the dependence is only of one attribute on another (e.g., will depends on knowledge), and there is no impossibility in that. The refutation replies that existence is not from the essence in the way attributes are, and if it were granted that existence depends on something, that would contradict the very definition of 'necessary by essence.' This shows the importance of distinguishing between essential attributes and existence itself.

Misconception: Some may think that 'by essence' means no attributes are needed at all, but the debate is specifically about whether baqa' is an additional attribute or identical to essence.
Correction: The passage clarifies that baqa' is not an added attribute; it is the same as the essence's necessary endurance. Other attributes like knowledge and will may depend on each other, but existence itself cannot be dependent.

Checkpoint

A) Baqa' is an additional attribute distinct from the essence.
B) Baqa' is by essence and not an additional attribute.

Key Takeaway
The essence of the Necessary Being includes endurance; it is not an added attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Will you consciously remind yourself that God's eternity is His very being, not something He possesses?
?
The objection in this passage suggests that it's okay for one attribute to depend on another (like will on knowledge). But the refutation shows that existence itself cannot depend on anything. In your own life, what are the things you tend to lean on for your sense of 'existence' or worth – your job, relationships, achievements? Would you still worry about what is to come, knowing that the One who holds all times is Himself timeless and self-sufficient? The Third Argument Against Baqa' as an Additional Attribute
Sanusi presents a reductio ad absurdum argument against baqa' as an additional attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third rational argument that negates baqa' being an additional attribute distinct from the divine essence.

Core Idea
Only self-subsistence avoids circularity, substitution, or multiplicity.

Sanusi now presents a sophisticated argument that examines three possible relationships between the divine essence and an assumed attribute of endurance. Each possibility leads to an absurdity, forcing the conclusion that the essence must be enduring by itself. This argument is a classic example of reductio ad absurdum in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation, to get a sense of the argument's flow without analysis.
Notice the three conditional scenarios signaled by 'if' (لو).
2
Identify the three possibilities
The passage examines three possibilities: baqa' depends on the essence, the essence depends on baqa', or neither depends on the other. Locate each in the text.
3
Understand each absurdity
For each possibility, see why it leads to circularity, substitution (خلف), or multiplicity of necessary beings (تعدد الواجب). The commentary will help clarify.
These are classical absurdities in kalam.
4
Grasp the conclusion
Realize that the only consistent position is that the essence endures by itself, without an additional attribute. The argument refutes the idea of baqa' as a separate entity.
This conclusion supports the Ash'ari position on divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وثالثها: أن الذات لو كان باقياً بالبقاء لا بنفسه، فإن افتقرصفة البقاء إلى الذات لزم الدور لتوقف ثبوت كل ما في الزمان الثاني على الآخر، وإن افتقر الذات إلى البقاء مع استغنائه عنه كان الواجب هو البقاء لا الذات هذا خلف، وإن لم يفتقر أحدهما على الآخر، بل اتفق تحققهما معاً كما ذكره صاحب المواقف لزم تعدد الواجب لأن كلا من الذات والبقاء يكون مستغنياً عما سواه، إذ لو افتقر البقاء إلى شيء لافتقر إلى الذات ضرورة افتقار الكل إليه والمستغني عن جميع ما سواه واجب قطعاً مع أن ما فرض من عدم افتقار البقاء إلى الذات محال، لأن افتقار الصفة إلى الذات ضروري.
And the third [argument] is that if the essence were enduring by baqa' and not by itself, then if the attribute of baqa' depends on the essence, circularity follows because the subsistence of each in the second time depends on the other; and if the essence depends on baqa' while being independent of it, then the necessary being would be baqa', not the essence—this is a contradiction; and if neither depends on the other, but they happen to exist together as the author of al-Mawāqif mentioned, then multiplicity of necessary beings follows, because each of the essence and baqa' would be independent of everything else, since if baqa' depended on something, it would depend on the essence necessarily because everything depends on it, and that which is independent of everything else is necessarily necessary, while the assumption of baqa' not depending on the essence is impossible, because the dependence of an attribute on the essence is necessary.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage presents the third argument against baqa' being an additional attribute distinct from the divine essence. It considers three possibilities: (1) If the attribute of baqa' depends on the essence, then circularity occurs because each would need the other for subsistence in the second time. (2) If the essence depends on baqa' while the essence is independent of baqa', then baqa' would be the necessary being, not the essence—a contradiction. (3) If neither depends on the other but they coincidentally exist together, then both would be independent of everything else, making each a necessary being, which implies a multiplicity of necessary beings—an impossibility. The argument then states that the assumption of baqa' not depending on the essence is impossible because attributes necessarily depend on the essence. This shows that the only consistent position is that the essence is enduring by itself, without an additional attribute.

Key Terms
بقاء
ذات
دور
خلف
تعدد الواجب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that an additional attribute like baqa' is necessary to explain God's enduring existence.
Correction: The argument shows that positing an additional attribute leads to logical absurdities; hence, the essence must be enduring by itself.

Checkpoint
What does the third argument conclude about baqa'?
A) Baqa' must be an additional attribute to avoid circularity.
B) The essence must be enduring by itself, not by an additional attribute.
C) Baqa' and the essence can be independent of each other.
D) There are multiple necessary beings.

Key Takeaway
The essence endures by itself; assuming an additional attribute of endurance leads to logical absurdities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever casually thought of God's attributes as if they were separate additions to His essence, like qualities added to a person? What does this lesson reveal about the danger of that subtle drift in your thinking? Will you correct it starting now?
?
If you truly affirm that God's essence endures by itself, how should that change the way you speak about His mercy, power, or anger? Are you willing to hold back from imagining them as independent forces and instead see them as inseparable from who He is?
?
The argument shows that assuming an additional attribute leads to absurdity. What other assumptions about God do you hold that, if examined, might lead to similar absurdities? Are you prepared to let go of them even if they are comfortable?

6 min
The Fourth Argument Against Baqa' as an Additional Attribute
Sanusi presents the fourth argument against baqa' being additional and its refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth argument against baqa' as an additional attribute, including the infinite regress and meaning-subsisting-in-meaning objections, and how the reply leads to denying all additional attributes.

Core Idea
If baqa' is additional, it creates infinite regress; if not, it's like a knower without knowledge.

Sanusi now presents the fourth argument against baqa' being an additional attribute. This argument is dialectical: it first shows the problems with positing an additional baqa', then considers an objection, and finally shows that the objection leads to an even more radical conclusion. By the end, you will see how this argument ties into the broader debate about divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: a conditional statement ('if baqa' were additional...'), then two branches (if it has baqa' / if it has no baqa'), then an objection and a reply.
This is a tightly reasoned argument; follow each step.
2
Analyze the two branches
The argument considers two possibilities if baqa' is additional: either it has its own baqa' (leading to infinite regress and qiyām al-maʿnā bi-l-maʿnā) or it does not (making it like a knower without knowledge). Identify the problem with each.
3
Examine the objection and reply
The opponent objects that baqa' is enduring by itself (its baqa' is itself). Note how Sanusi replies: if that is allowed, then God can be enduring by a baqa' that is Himself, denying all additional attributes.
This reply turns the objection against the opponent.
4
Connect to the broader theology
Reflect on the conclusion: the argument shows that Ash'arī insistence on additional attributes can be undermined if baqa' is treated as self-subsisting. This ties into the Ahl al-Haqq position.
The lesson ends with a reference to 'the shaykh' and 'Ahl al-Haqq'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ورابعها أن البقاء لو كانت صفة أزلية زائدة على الذات قائمة به كانت باقية بالضرورة، وحينئذ فإن كان لها بقاء ينقل الكلام إليه بتسلسل وأيضاً يلزم قيام المعنى بالمعنى وهو باطل عندكم ، وإن لم يكن لها بقاء كان كعالم بلا علم وقد بين بطلانه . فإن قيل : هو باق بالبقاء إلا أن بقاءه نفسه لا زائداً عليه ليتسلسل قلنا : فحينئذ يجوز أن يكون الباري تعالى باقياً ببقاء هو نفسه عالماً بعلم هو نفسه، فلا يثبت زيادة صفة البقاء على ما هو رأي الشيخ ولا زيادة العلم والقدرة وغيرهما على ما هو رأي أهل الحق.
And the fourth [argument] is that if baqa' were an eternal attribute additional to the essence subsisting in it, then it would necessarily be enduring. Then, if it has a baqa', the discussion transfers to it ad infinitum, and also it necessitates the subsistence of a meaning in a meaning, which is invalid according to you; and if it has no baqa', it would be like a knower without knowledge, whose falsity has been shown. If it is said: It is enduring by baqa', but its baqa' is itself, not additional to it, to avoid the infinite regress. We say: Then it is permissible that the Exalted Creator is enduring by a baqa' that is Himself, knowing by a knowledge that is Himself; thus the additional attribute of baqa' is not established according to the view of the shaykh, nor the addition of knowledge, power, and others according to the view of Ahl al-Haqq.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth argument against baqa' being an additional attribute. It argues that if baqa' is an eternal attribute additional to the essence, then baqa' itself must be enduring. Then it considers two options: if baqa' has its own baqa', that leads to an infinite regress and also the problem of 'a meaning subsisting in a meaning' (qiyām al-maʿnā bi-l-maʿnā), which is invalid in Ashʿarī thought. If baqa' has no baqa', then it would be like a knower without knowledge, which is false. The opponent might reply that baqa' endures by itself (its baqa' is itself), avoiding regress. The response is that if that is allowed, then we can say the same for the Creator: He endures by a baqa' that is Himself and knows by a knowledge that is Himself, which would negate the additional attributes entirely—this is the position of the Shaykh (Abū al-Ḥasan al-Ashʿarī) and Ahl al-Sunna. Thus the argument attempts to show that the opponent's move leads to the denial of additional attributes altogether.

Key Terms
بقاء

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that saying 'baqa' is itself' solves the problem without consequences.
Correction: The passage shows that this move leads to denying all additional attributes, which contradicts the Ash'arī position, so it does not salvage the view.

Checkpoint
What does the fourth argument say about baqa' if it is an additional attribute?
A) It must have its own baqa', leading to infinite regress.
B) It need not be enduring.
C) It is the same as the essence.
D) It is independent of the essence.

Key Takeaway
The fourth argument shows that positing baqa' as an additional attribute leads to either infinite regress or absurdity, and the objection that baqa' is itself only undermines the case for any additional attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that God's attributes are not separate from His essence, does that change how you perceive His closeness to you? How does it affect your worship to know that His knowledge, power, and endurance are identical to His very being?
?
The opponent's objection seemed reasonable at first, but led to denying all attributes. Are there beliefs you hold that seem reasonable but, if followed to their logical conclusion, would undermine your faith? Will you examine your own assumptions today?
?
This argument exposes the danger of trying to defend a position without seeing where it leads. Is there any area of your life where you are defending a comfortable belief without considering its full implications? Will you ask Allah to show you the truth, even if it is uncomfortable?

Divine Attributes
beginner
5 min
The Objection to Attribute Endurance and a Rejected Solution
Objection and first rejected solution to attribute endurance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that eternal attributes cannot endure without an additional attribute, and why the proposal to simply avoid attributing endurance to them fails.

Core Idea
Eternal attributes must endure, but a 'solution' that denies their endurance is self-defeating.

Sanusi presents a strong objection to the earlier claim that the attributes are identical to the essence. If they are distinct, how can they be eternal without an infinite chain of attributes? The first proposed solution—to say attributes are not enduring—is quickly shown to be impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
The objection argues that eternal attributes like knowledge and power are necessarily enduring, yet they cannot have an additional baqa' (endurance) because that would lead to a meaning subsisting in a meaning and a multiplicity of eternal entities. Understand the logical dilemma.
The objection builds on the earlier proof that attributes are not identical to the essence.
2
Identify the first solution
Some early scholars proposed that we only say the essence endures with its attributes, but we do not say the attributes themselves are enduring. This attempts to sidestep the problem.
This solution is presented and then immediately refuted.
3
Understand the refutation
Sanusi states that the falsity of this solution is clear because an eternal attribute's endurance is necessary (ضروري). Denying it would contradict the nature of eternal attributes.
This refutation shows that the problem cannot be dismissed so lightly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعترض على هذا الجواب بأن كون بقاء الباري أو علمه أو قدرته نفس ذاته محال لما مر في إثبات الصفات بخلاف كون بقاء البقاء كوجود الوجود وقدم القدم وغير ذلك، فأورد الإشكال ببقاء الصفات، فإن العلم القديم باق بالضرورة، وكذا سائر الصفات مع امتناع أن يكون البقاء نفس العلم والقدرة وغيرهما فلزم قيام المعنى بالمعنى وثبوت قدماء أخر لم يقل بها أحد وللقوم في التقصي عن هذا الإشكال وجوه : الأول : لبعض القدماء أنا نقول الذات باق بصفاته ولا نقول الصفات باقية ليلزم المحال وفساده بين لأن كون الصفة الأزلية باقية ضروري. الثاني : لبعض الأشاعرة وينسب إلى الشيخ أن العلم باق ببقاء هو نفس العلم ، وكذا سائر الصفات كما ذكر في البقاء وأوضحه الأستاذ بأنه لما ثبت قدم الصفات ولزم كونها باقية وامتنع الباقي بلا بقاء وكونها باقية ببقاء زائد لاستحالة قيام المعنى بالمعنى، ثبت أن كلاً منها باقية ببقاء هو نفسها فكان العلم مثلاً صفة للذات بها يكون الذات عالماً، وبقاء لنفسه به يكون هو باقياً، وكان بقاء الذات بقاء له، وبقاء لنفسه أيضاً، ولم يكن العلم صفة لنفسه حتى يلزم كونه عالماً، وهذا كما أن الجسم كائن في المكان بكون يخصه ويزيد عليه ضرورة تحقق هذا الجسم بدون هذا التمكن ، ثم هذا الكون كائن بكون هو نفسه لا زائد عليه، قائم به ، ولم يكن العلم علماً لنفسه حتى يلزم كونه عالماً، ولا بقاؤه بقاء للذات ليلزم كونه عالماً باقياً بشيء واحد. فإن قيل : فقد لزم كون الذات عالماً بما هو بقاء، والعلم باقياً بما هو علم وهو محال . قلنا: المستحيل أن يكون الشيء عالماً بما هو بقاء له، وباقياً بما هو علم له وها هنا العلم علم للذات وليسا بقاء له، والبقاء بقاء للعلم، وليس علماً له.
And an objection was raised against this answer: that the baqa' of the Creator, or His knowledge, or His power being His very essence is impossible, as was mentioned in the proof of attributes, unlike the case of the baqa' of baqa' like the existence of existence and the eternity of eternity and so forth. Thus the difficulty was posed regarding the endurance of attributes: for eternal knowledge is necessarily enduring, and likewise the rest of the attributes, while it is impossible that baqa' is the same as knowledge and power and others, so it necessitates the subsistence of a meaning in a meaning and the establishment of other eternal entities that no one has held. And the scholars have ways to extricate themselves from this difficulty: The first: from some early scholars: we say the essence is enduring with its attributes, and we do not say the attributes are enduring, so that the impossibility attaches; but its falsity is clear because the eternal attribute being enduring is necessary. The second: from some Ash'aris, attributed to the Shaykh, that knowledge is enduring by a baqa' that is knowledge itself, and likewise the rest of the attributes, as mentioned regarding baqa'; and the master elucidated this: Since the attributes are proven eternal and necessarily enduring, and it is impossible for an enduring thing to be without baqa' and for it to be enduring by an additional baqa' due to the impossibility of a meaning subsisting in a meaning, it is established that each of them is enduring by a baqa' that is itself. For example, knowledge is an attribute of the essence by which the essence is knowing, and it is baqa' for itself by which it is enduring; and the baqa' of the essence is baqa' for it, and also baqa' for itself; and knowledge was not an attribute of itself so as to necessitate its being knowing. This is like a body being 'in place' by a spatial mode specific to it and additional to it, because the body can exist without this spatial mode; then this spatial mode is 'in place' by a spatial mode that is itself, not additional to it, subsisting in it; and knowledge was not knowledge of itself so as to necessitate its being knowing, nor was its baqa' a baqa' for the essence so as to necessitate its being knowing and enduring by one thing. If it is said: Then it necessitates that the essence is knowing by virtue of being baqa', and knowledge is enduring by virtue of being knowledge, which is impossible. We say: The impossible is that something should be knowing by virtue of being baqa' for it, and enduring by virtue of being knowledge for it; whereas here knowledge is knowledge for the essence and is not baqa' for it, and baqa' is baqa' for knowledge and is not knowledge for it.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage presents an objection to the previous answer and then gives three solutions (wujuh) to the problem of how eternal attributes (like knowledge, power) can be enduring without requiring an additional attribute of baqa'. The objection argues that if the Creator's baqa', knowledge, and power were identical to the essence, that would contradict the earlier proof establishing distinct attributes; however, the problem is that eternal attributes must be enduring, but they cannot have an additional baqa' because that would lead to 'a meaning subsisting in a meaning' and multiplicity of eternal entities. The first solution, from some early scholars, simply states that the essence endures with its attributes but the attributes themselves are not said to be enduring—but this is rejected because it is necessary that eternal attributes endure. The second solution, from some Ash'aris attributed to al-Ash'ari, states that each attribute is enduring by a baqa' that is itself. The author explains this with an analogy: a body is 'in place' by a spatial mode (kawn) that is additional to the body, but that spatial mode itself is 'in place' by a spatial mode that is itself, not additional. Similarly, knowledge is an attribute of the essence but its baqa' is itself, so it doesn't require an external attribute to endure. Then there is a further objection that this would make the essence knowing by virtue of being baqa', etc., which is answered by distinguishing functions: knowledge is for the essence, baqa' is for knowledge; there is no overlap. The passage carefully defends the Ash'ari position that attributes are eternal and self-subsistent in a sense.

Key Terms
بقاء الصفات
قيام المعنى بالمعنى
قدماء أخر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that we can avoid the problem by not attributing endurance to attributes, saying only the essence endures with them.
Correction: But eternal attributes by definition must be enduring; denying that is impossible.

Checkpoint
Why is the first solution (that we do not say attributes are enduring) rejected?
A) Because it leads to an infinite regress.
B) Because eternal attributes are necessarily enduring.
C) Because it implies the attributes are identical to the essence.
D) Because it contradicts the earlier proof.

Key Takeaway
Eternal attributes must be enduring; any solution that denies their endurance is invalid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were presented with a theological 'shortcut' that denies a necessary truth about Allah's attributes, would you be tempted to accept it for simplicity? What does that reveal about your priorities?
?
This lesson shows that denying attribute endurance is not just wrong but self-contradictory. Is there an area of your faith where you have accepted a belief that contradicts a necessary truth because it felt more convenient? Will you re-examine it now?
?
The early scholars' solution seemed plausible but was rejected. Have you ever clung to a comfortable but incorrect understanding of a divine attribute? How can you commit yourself to accepting what is necessarily true about Allah, even when it challenges your intellect?

Divine Attributes
beginner

The Ash'ari Solution: Attributes Endure by Themselves
Second Ash'ari solution to attribute endurance with analogy and defense.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari argument that each eternal attribute endures by a baqa' identical to itself, and the defense against objections using an analogy.

Core Idea
Each attribute is self-enduring, just as a body's spatial mode is itself spatial by itself.

The second solution, attributed to al-Ash'ari, avoids infinite regress by claiming that each attribute's endurance is identical to the attribute itself. Sanusi elaborates with an analogy of a body and its spatial mode, and then answers an objection concerning overlap of functions.

Guided Path
1
Read the second solution
The solution states that knowledge is enduring by a baqa' that is knowledge itself, and similarly for other attributes. This avoids an additional attribute of endurance.
This is attributed to some Ash'aris and to al-Ash'ari himself.
2
Examine the analogy
Sanusi draws an analogy: a body is 'in place' by a spatial mode (kawn) that is additional to the body, but that spatial mode itself is 'in place' by a spatial mode that is itself, not additional. Similarly, each attribute's baqa' is itself.
The analogy clarifies how something can be both an attribute and its own endurance.
3
Address the objection
An objection is raised that this would make the essence knowing by virtue of being baqa', and knowledge enduring by virtue of being knowledge. The answer distinguishes functions: knowledge is for the essence, baqa' is for knowledge; there is no overlap.
This preserves the distinct roles while avoiding contradiction.

Source Text

?

?

?
If you truly believe God’s attributes endure by themselves without need of an external baqa', does this increase your awe of His self-sufficiency? How might this affect your reliance on created means versus trust in His direct attributes?

Divine Attributes

The Objection and the First Failed Solution on Baqa
Presents an objection against identifying baqa with the essence and the first failed solution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical objection against identifying the attribute of remaining (baqa) with the essence and why the first proposed solution—denying that attributes remain—is self-contradictory.

Core Idea
Eternal attributes must remain, so denying their remaining is self-contradictory.

Theologians faced a puzzle: if remaining is an attribute, and it cannot be identical to the essence, then it seems to subsist in another attribute, leading to multiple eternal entities. The first attempted solution—to say attributes do not remain—was quickly rejected as obviously false. This passage presents the objection and the first of three proposed solutions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the first part of the passage where the objector argues that if baqa is identical to the essence, then knowledge, power, etc. would also have to be identical, which is impossible. This forces a difficulty: attributes are eternal and must be 'remaining', but remaining cannot be the same as the attribute itself.
Notice the key consequence: qiyam al-ma'na bi al-ma'na (subsistence of a meaning in a meaning) and affirmation of multiple eternal entities.
2
Identify the first proposed solution
Some early scholars proposed that the essence remains with its attributes, but the attributes themselves do not remain. Find this in the passage.
3
Analyze why it fails
The author immediately rejects this as evident falsity. Ask yourself: why is it necessary for an eternal attribute to be remaining? Think about the definition of eternity: it implies perpetuity and remaining.
This is linked to the core idea.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعترض على هذا الجواب بأن كون بقاء الباري أو علمه أو قدرته نفس ذاته محال لما مر في إثبات الصفات بخلاف كون بقاء البقاء كوجود الوجود وقدم القدم وغير ذلك، فأورد الإشكال ببقاء الصفات، فإن العلم القديم باق بالضرورة، وكذا سائر الصفات مع امتناع أن يكون البقاء نفس العلم والقدرة وغيرهما فلزم قيام المعنى بالمعنى وثبوت قدماء أخر لم يقل بها أحد وللقوم في التقصي عن هذا الإشكال وجوه : الأول : لبعض القدماء أنا نقول الذات باق بصفاته ولا نقول الصفات باقية ليلزم المحال وفساده بين لأن كون الصفة الأزلية باقية ضروري.
And it was objected to this answer that the state of the remaining (baqa') of the Lord, or His knowledge, or His power being the very essence itself is impossible, due to what has passed in the proof of attributes, unlike the state of the remaining of remaining [i.e., the existence of the attribute of remaining] like the existence of existence, and the oldness of eternity, etc. So the difficulty was raised concerning the remaining of the attributes. For the eternal knowledge is necessarily remaining, and likewise the rest of the attributes, while it is impossible for remaining to be identical to knowledge, power, etc. Therefore it necessitated the subsistence of a meaning in a meaning (qiyam al-ma'na bi al-ma'na) and the affirmation of other eternal entities (qudama') that no one has asserted. And there are ways (wujuh) for the people to extricate themselves from this difficulty: The first: Some of the early scholars say: We say the essence (dhat) remains with its attributes, and we do not say the attributes remain, so that the impossible does not follow. But its falsity is evident because the eternal attribute being remaining is necessary.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage begins by stating an objection to a previous answer (presumably that the attribute of remaining is identical to the essence). The objector argues that if remaining is identical to the essence, then knowledge, power, etc. would also have to be identical to the essence, which is impossible. The objection concludes that a difficulty arises: eternal attributes must be 'remaining' (i.e., they persist), but remaining cannot be the same as the attributes themselves, because that would entail that a meaning subsists in a meaning (qiyam al-ma'na bi al-ma'na), leading to multiple eternal entities. The text then introduces three 'ways' (wujuh) to resolve this difficulty. The first way is from some early scholars: they propose that only the essence remains with its attributes, but the attributes themselves do not remain. The author immediately rejects this as self-evidently false ('fasaduhu bayyin'), because an eternal attribute is necessarily remaining by its very nature.

Key Terms
بقاء (baqa')
ذات (dhat)
صفات (sifat)
قيام المعنى بالمعنى (qiyam al-ma'na bi al-ma'na)
قدماء (qudama')

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that denying the remaining of attributes avoids the problem of qiyam al-ma'na bi al-ma'na.
Correction: The author shows this contradicts the necessity of eternity: an eternal attribute must be remaining, so denying its remaining is self-contradictory.

Checkpoint
Why did the early scholars' suggestion that 'the essence remains with its attributes but the attributes do not remain' fail?
A) It leads to an infinite regress
B) An eternal attribute must be remaining, so denying its remaining is self-contradictory
C) It affirms multiple eternal entities
D) It contradicts the proof of the attributes' existence

Key Takeaway
The first attempted solution—denying that attributes remain—fails because it contradicts the necessary nature of eternal attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God’s attributes are eternally remaining without change, how does that challenge your comfort with moments when you feel God’s mercy or knowledge are distant? Are you willing to ask Him to realign your heart with this unchanging truth today?
?
The early scholars feared that affirming remaining attributes might lead to multiplicity. Have you ever avoided a truthful belief about God because it felt uncomfortable to your understanding of tawhid? What would it cost you to accept what reason and revelation demand, even if it unsettles you?
?
Consider a time you doubted God’s constancy. Which of His attributes felt fragile to you? How does the necessity that eternal attributes are necessarily remaining force you to reconsider that doubt? Will you take a moment now to repent for any wavering in your heart and reaffirm your trust in His permanent attributes?

Divine Attributes
