The Second Solution: Attributes Self-Remaining
Explains the Ash'ari view that each attribute remains by a remaining identical to itself, with an objection and answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari argument that each divine attribute remains by a remaining identical to itself, and how they respond to the objection that this leads to cross-category confusion.

Core Idea
Each attribute remains by itself, not by an additional attribute.

Having established the necessity of remaining for the divine attributes, the issue arises: how can an attribute be 'remaining' without a separate remaining attribute? The second solution presents a bold claim: each attribute is its own remaining. This raises subtle issues about the relations between the essence, the attribute, and the attribute's remaining, which the text resolves with a careful distinction and an analogy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation once to get the overall flow. Note the key terms: 'بقاء' (remaining), 'علم' (knowledge), 'ذات' (essence).
This is a dense argument; don't worry about every detail at first.
2
Identify the core argument
Find the statement that knowledge is remaining by a remaining that is itself. Notice the reasoning: because an additional remaining would lead to 'qiyam al-ma'na bi al-ma'na' (subsistence of a meaning in a meaning).
The analogy with a body's 'being' (kawn) helps clarify.
3
Understand the objection
The objector claims that if knowledge is self-remaining, then the essence would be knowing by what is a remaining, and knowledge would be remaining by what is knowledge—a cross-category confusion. Find this objection in the text.
4
Analyze the answer
The answer distinguishes: knowledge is an attribute for the essence (making it knowing) but not a remaining for it; remaining is an attribute for knowledge (making it remaining) but not knowledge for it. See how this avoids the absurdity.
The distinction is subtle but crucial.
5
Reflect on the analogy
Compare with the body-kawn example: the body has a 'being' that is additional to it, but that 'being' itself is 'being' by its own 'being'. This parallels the attribute's self-remaining.
This analogy helps grasp the concept of self-remaining.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : لبعض الأشاعرة وينسب إلى الشيخ أن العلم باق ببقاء هو نفس العلم ، وكذا سائر الصفات كما ذكر في البقاء وأوضحه الأستاذ بأنه لما ثبت قدم الصفات ولزم كونها باقية وامتنع الباقي بلا بقاء وكونها باقية ببقاء زائد لاستحالة قيام المعنى بالمعنى، ثبت أن كلاً منها باقية ببقاء هو نفسها فكان العلم مثلاً صفة للذات بها يكون الذات عالماً، وبقاء لنفسه به يكون هو باقياً، وكان بقاء الذات بقاء له، وبقاء لنفسه أيضاً، ولم يكن العلم صفة لنفسه حتى يلزم كونه عالماً، وهذا كما أن الجسم كائن في المكان بكون يخصه ويزيد عليه ضرورة تحقق هذا الجسم بدون هذا التمكن ، ثم هذا الكون كائن بكون هو نفسه لا زائد عليه، قائم به ، ولم يكن العلم علماً لنفسه حتى يلزم كونه عالماً، ولا بقاؤه بقاء للذات ليلزم كونه عالماً باقياً بشيء واحد . فإن قيل : فقد لزم كون الذات عالماً بما هو بقاء، والعلم باقياً بما هو علم وهو محال . قلنا: المستحيل أن يكون الشيء عالماً بما هو بقاء له، وباقياً بما هو علم له وها هنا العلم علم للذات وليسا بقاء له، والبقاء بقاء للعلم، وليس علماً له.
The second: Some Ash'aris—and it is attributed to the Shaykh—that knowledge is remaining by a remaining that is the very knowledge itself, and likewise the rest of the attributes, as mentioned in the section on remaining (al-baqa'), and the master (al-ustadh) clarified it: because when the eternalness of the attributes is established and it is necessary that they be remaining, and it is impossible for something remaining to be without a remaining, and for them to be remaining by an additional remaining due to the impossibility of the subsistence of a meaning in a meaning, it is established that each of them is remaining by a remaining that is itself. Thus, for example, knowledge is an attribute of the essence by which the essence is knowing, and it is a remaining for itself by which it is remaining. And the remaining of the essence is a remaining for it (the essence), and also a remaining for itself (knowledge). And knowledge was not an attribute of itself such that it would be necessary for it to be knowing; and this is like how a body is 'being in a place' (ka'in) by a 'being' (kawn) that is specific to it and additional to it, due to the necessity of this body being realized without this locating (tamakkun); then this 'being' (kawn) is 'being' (ka'in) by a 'being' (kawn) that is itself, not additional to it, subsisting in it. And knowledge was not knowledge for itself so that it would be necessary for it to be knowing, nor was its remaining a remaining for the essence so that it would be necessary for the essence to be knowing and remaining by a single thing. If it is said: Then it is necessary that the essence be knowing by virtue of what is a remaining, and knowledge be remaining by virtue of what is knowledge, and that is impossible. We say: The impossible is that a thing be knowing by virtue of what is a remaining for it, and remaining by virtue of what is knowledge for it. But here, knowledge is knowledge for the essence, not a remaining for it; and remaining is remaining for knowledge, not knowledge for it.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage presents the second of three proposed solutions to the earlier difficulty. It is attributed to some Ash'aris and to the Shaykh (likely Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari). The argument is: Since the attributes are eternal, they must be 'remaining' (baqiya). But remaining cannot be an additional attribute because that would involve a meaning subsisting in a meaning (qiyam al-ma'na bi al-ma'na). Therefore, each attribute must be remaining by a remaining that is identical to itself. For example, knowledge is both an attribute of the essence (by which the essence is knowing) and a remaining for itself (by which it remains). The writer draws an analogy with a body and its 'being in a place' (kawn): the body has a specific 'being' that is additional to it, but then that 'being' itself is 'being' by its own 'being' without an additional one. Then an objection is raised: This would imply that the essence is knowing by what is the remaining (baqa') of knowledge, and knowledge is remaining by what is its knowledge—a cross-category confusion. The answer clarifies the distinction: knowledge is an attribute for the essence (making it knowing) but not a remaining for it; remaining is an attribute for knowledge (making it remaining) but not knowledge for it. Thus no absurdity follows.

Key Terms
بقاء (baqa')
علم ('ilm)
ذات (dhat)
كون (kawn)
قيام المعنى بالمعنى (qiyam al-ma'na bi al-ma'na)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if knowledge is self-remaining, then the essence would be knowing by the same thing that makes knowledge remain, leading to a contradiction.
Correction: The text clarifies that knowledge's being an attribute of the essence (making it knowing) and its being a remaining for itself are two distinct relations; they do not cross over.

Checkpoint
According to the second solution, how is knowledge related to its own remaining?
A) Knowledge is remaining by an additional remaining
B) Knowledge is remaining by a remaining that is identical to itself
C) Knowledge does not have a remaining
D) Knowledge remains by the remaining of the essence

Key Takeaway
The second solution resolves the problem of attribute-remaining by asserting that each attribute is its own remaining, avoiding infinite regress while carefully distinguishing between the attribute's function for the essence and its own subsistence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you struggle to understand a precise theological distinction like the one in this lesson, do you tend to rush to reject it as convoluted, or do you humble yourself and study it carefully? What will you do the next time you encounter a difficult theological point?
?
The objection in this lesson shows how easy it is to misunderstand and make a false inference. Have you ever dismissed a nuanced explanation of Allah's attributes because it seemed 'philosophical' or 'confusing,' only later to realize your own neglect? How can you train yourself to withhold judgment until you fully grasp the distinctions being made?

The Burden of Proof in the Debate on Divine Attributes
Raises objection that if attributes can be self-remaining, then essence could be self-knowing; response and counter-objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'ari response to the objection that the essence could be self-knowing involves the principles of attribute increase and the non-multiplicity of eternal entities.

Core Idea
The burden of proof shifts: the default is no multiple eternal entities unless proven.

This passage presents a dialectical exchange following the solution that knowledge is self-remaining. The objector seizes this to argue for the Mu'tazilite position that attributes are identical to the essence. The response involves two key principles: the original principle of attribute increase (ziyada al-sifa) and the original principle of non-multiplicity of eternal entities (qudama). By the end, the defender turns the tables, placing the burden of proof on those who posit additional attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Identify the objector's argument: if knowledge can be self-remaining, then why can't the essence be self-knowing? This is the Mu'tazilite position that attributes are identical to the essence.
The objector is using the defender's own solution against him.
2
Follow the response and counter-objection
The defender first refers to earlier corruptions. Then a refined objection follows: if knowledge's remaining is its own self, why can't the essence's remaining be its own self without an additional attribute? Note the defender's two arguments: the preventer (subsistence of meaning in meaning) and the original principle of non-multiplicity.
The defender gives two distinct responses.
3
Reflect on the dialectical structure
Notice how the burden of proof is shifted. The defender uses a 'mu'arada' (countering) by invoking a different original principle. This shows the complexity and subtlety of kalam argumentation.
The debate hinges on which default principle is accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : إذا جاز كون العلم باقياً ببقاء هو نفسه، فلم لا يجوز كون الذات عالماً بعلم هو نفسه، قادراً بقدرة هي نفسه إلى غير ذلك على ما هو رأي المعتزلة . قلنا : لما سبق في بحث زيادة الصفات من لزوم الفسادات ويرد على هذا الوجه أنه إذا جاز أن يكون بقاء العلم نفسه، فلم لا يجوز أن يكون بقاء الذات نفسه، ولا تثبت صفة زائدة؟ فإن قيل : الأصل زيادة الصفة إلا لمانع ، وهو ها هنا لزوم قيام المعنى بالمعنى، ولم يوجد في بقاء الذات . قلنا : خطأ ومعارضة بأن الأصل عدم تكثر القدماء إلا لقاطع .
If it is said: Since it is permissible for knowledge to be remaining by a remaining that is itself, then why is it not permissible for the essence to be knowing by a knowledge that is itself, powerful by a power that is itself, and so on, according to the view of the Mu'tazila? We say: Due to what has passed in the discussion of the increase (ziyada) of the attributes, of the occurrence of corruptions (fasadat). And it is objected to this face (al-wajh) that if it is permissible for the remaining of knowledge to be itself, then why is it not permissible for the remaining of the essence to be itself, and no additional attribute is established? If it is said: The original principle (asl) is the increase of the attribute except where there is a preventer (mani'), and here it is the necessity of the subsistence of a meaning in a meaning, and that does not exist in the case of the remaining of the essence. We say: Error, and it is countered (mu'arada) that the original principle is the non-multiplicity of eternal entities (qudama') except with a decisive proof (qati').
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage begins with a new objection: If the second solution allows knowledge to be self-remaining, then why not also allow the essence to be self-knowing, self-powerful, etc., which is the Mu'tazilite position? The answer first refers back to the earlier discussion on the increase of attributes, which concluded that such a view leads to corruptions. However, the objector then turns the argument around: If knowledge can have its own remaining identical to itself, then why can't the essence have its own remaining identical to itself, without an additional attribute? The defender responds with two points: first, that the original principle (al-asl) is that attributes are additional unless prevented—and here the preventer (subsistence of meaning in meaning) applies to attributes but not to the essence's self-remaining. Second, the defender counters that the original principle is actually the non-multiplicity of eternal entities unless a decisive proof introduces multiplicity. Thus, the burden of proof is on those who posit additional attributes. This is a dialectical exchange showing the complexity of the debate.

Key Terms
زيادة الصفات (ziyada al-sifat)
أصل (asl)
مانع (mani')
قيام المعنى بالمعنى (qiyam al-ma'na bi al-ma'na)
تكثر القدماء (takaththur al-qudama')

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The defender is inconsistent for allowing attributes to be self-remaining while denying the same for the essence.
Correction: The defender argues that a different preventer (subsistence of meaning in meaning) applies to attributes but not to the essence's self-remaining, and moreover the burden of proof is on those who posit multiple eternal entities.

Checkpoint
In the response to the objection, what is given as the 'original principle' (al-asl) regarding the increase of attributes?
A) The original principle is that the essence has no attributes
B) The original principle is that attributes are additional unless prevented
C) The original principle is that attributes are identical to the essence
D) The original principle is that eternal entities must be multiple

Key Takeaway
The defender shifts the burden of proof by invoking the original principle of non-multiplicity of eternal entities, thereby requiring decisive proof for additional attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The defender shifts the burden of proof to those who assert multiple eternal entities. In your own understanding of Allah, do you sometimes unconsciously multiply causes or explanations when the simpler default (tawhid) should suffice? How can you actively practice the principle of non-multiplicity in your daily thoughts about Allah's oneness?
?
When you encounter theological disagreements, which 'original principle' do you instinctively gravitate towards—the default that something is added, or the default that it is not? What does your instinct reveal about your trust in God's simplicity?
?
Are you willing to accept a theological truth simply because it is the 'default' position, even if you do not fully understand the preventing factor? How does that reflect your humility before the scholars and your reliance on revelation?

Divine Attributes

al-Ash'ari's Third Solution: Attributes Remain by the Essence's Remaining
Presents al-Ash'ari's third solution and its criticism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ash'ari's third solution for the persistence of divine attributes and the key criticism that attributes are neither other than nor identical to the essence.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari says attributes remain by the essence's remaining, but criticism says they are neither other nor identical.

This lesson presents the third solution from al-Ash'ari himself on the persistence of divine attributes. He argues that attributes remain by the same remaining as the essence because there is no real distinction between them. However, a significant criticism emerges: the attributes are neither wholly other than the essence nor identical to it, raising problems for the solution.

Guided Path
1
Read and identify parts
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Identify three sections: al-Ash'ari's solution, the criticism, and the response to an objection.
Notice the structure: solution given, then 'wa yuriddu 'alayhi' introduces the criticism, then 'Amma al-i'tirad' introduces the objection response.
2
Understand the solution
Focus on al-Ash'ari's claim: attributes are remaining by baqa' al-dhat (remaining of the essence) because there is no mughayara (difference) between essence and attributes. Compare with substance and accidents where there is difference.
The contrast with jawhar and a'rad is crucial: for substance, its remaining is not the essence's remaining.
3
Analyze the criticism
The criticism states that attributes are neither ghayr al-dhat nor 'ayn al-dhat. If they are not identical, then an attribute subsisting in what is not the essence itself is problematic. Grasp the dilemma.
This criticism challenges the very possibility of attributes remaining by the essence's remaining.
4
Examine the rebuttal
The text rebuts an objection: if attributes remain by the essence's remaining, then they would be knowing or powerful. The rebuttal says that is not established; knowledge is remaining but not powerful.
The objection is dismissed as not following from the solution because it assumes something not proven.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثالث للأشعري : أن الصفات باقية ببقاء هو بقاء الذات، وجاز ذلك لعدم المغايرة بين الذات والصفات بخلاف الجوهر مع أعراضه فلذا لم يكن بقاؤه بقاء . ويرد عليه أن الصفات كما أنها ليست غير الذات فليست عينه أيضاً، وكما امتنع اتصاف الشيء بصفة قائمة بالغير فكذا بصفة قائمة بما ليس نفس ذلك الشيء. وأما الاعتراض بأنه لو كانت الصفات باقية ببقاء الذات لعدم التغاير لكانت عالمة بعلمه قادرة بقدرته إلى غير ذلك فليس بشيء لأن ذلك فرع صحة (1) من الانصاف وقد صح كون العلم مثلاً باقياً بخلاف كونه قادراً .
The third face (wajh) of al-Ash'ari: That the attributes are remaining by a remaining that is the remaining of the essence, and that is permissible due to the lack of difference (mughayara) between the essence and the attributes, unlike the substance (jawhar) with its accidents (a'rad), for which its remaining is not the [essence's] remaining. And it is objected to it that just as the attributes are not other than the essence, so too they are not identical to it ('ayn) either; and just as it is impossible for a thing to be described by an attribute subsisting in another, so too is it impossible [to be described] by an attribute subsisting in that which is not the very same thing. As for the objection that if the attributes were remaining by the remaining of the essence due to lack of difference, then they would be knowing by His knowledge, powerful by His power, etc., that is nothing, because that is subsidiary to the soundness (sihha) of fairness (al-insaf) and it is established that, for example, knowledge is remaining, unlike its being powerful.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage introduces the third solution from al-Ash'ari himself. He argues that the attributes remain by the same remaining as the essence (baqa' al-dhat), and this is possible because there is no real difference (mughayara) between the essence and its attributes—unlike a substance and its accidents, which are distinct. Then a criticism is offered: the attributes are neither wholly other than the essence nor identical to it. Therefore, an attribute cannot subsist in something that is not the same as the essence. The text then addresses a potential objection: if the attributes share the essence's remaining, then they would also share its knowledge, power, etc. But this is rejected because that would require the attribute to be knowing, which is not established. The author notes that it is established for knowledge to be remaining but not for it to be powerful.

Key Terms
بقاء الذات (baqa' al-dhat)
مغايرة (mughayara)
جوهر (jawhar)
عرض ('arad)
عين ('ayn)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if attributes are not other than the essence, they are identical to it.
Correction: The criticism explicitly states that attributes are neither other than the essence nor identical to it; they have a unique relationship.

Checkpoint
What is the main criticism of al-Ash'ari's third solution?
A) It leads to the attributes being unable to remain
B) The attributes are neither other than the essence nor identical to it, so they cannot be described by a remaining subsisting in the essence
C) It makes the essence multiple
D) It contradicts the necessity of remaining

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's solution that attributes remain by the essence's remaining is challenged by the insight that attributes are neither other than nor identical to the essence, making the relationship more complex.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that even al-Ash'ari's reasoning was challenged, how does that test your trust in intellectual formulations about Allah? Are you willing to hold your theological beliefs with humility, knowing that the most profound minds struggled with these questions?
?
The passage teaches that Allah's attributes are neither other than nor identical to Him. How does this affect your worship? Do you sometimes treat His mercy or power as separate entities rather than aspects of His very being? What would change in your dua if you truly internalized this?
?
Al-Ash'ari sought to preserve the continuity of Allah's attributes. Reflect: in your life, do you ever act as if Allah's attributes change based on your circumstances? How can you cultivate an unshakable trust in the eternal, unchanging nature of His attributes, even when life feels uncertain?

Initial Mu'tazila Objection and Response on Divine Attributes
Dialectical exchange on unity of attributes and essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila objection that if knowledge is eternal by itself, then the essence could be knowing by itself, and the theological response to this argument.

Core Idea
Attributes cannot be identical to the essence without leading to absurdities.

This passage presents a key dialectical exchange on the nature of divine attributes. The Mu'tazila challenge the Ash'ari position by arguing from analogy: if knowledge can be eternal by an eternity that is itself, why can't the essence be knowing by a knowledge that is itself? The response appeals to earlier arguments about the corruption that follows from denying attribute distinction. A further objection about the eternity of the essence is also addressed. This lesson unpacks the first half of this debate.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazila objection
Read the first objection: if knowledge's eternity is itself, then why can't the essence be knowing by a knowledge that is its very self? This is a reductio against the Ash'ari position.
The Mu'tazila aim to show that the Ash'ari reasoning leads to their own view.
2
Analyze the response
The response references a previous discussion about the 'corruptions' (fasadat) that follow from denying the increase of attributes. This is a shorthand for earlier arguments.
The Ash'ari rely on the principle that attributes are additional to the essence.
3
Examine the counter-objection
A second objection argues: if the eternity of knowledge is itself, then why can't the essence's eternity be itself, eliminating the need for an attribute?
This challenges the need for a separate attribute of eternity.
4
Assess the final reply
The reply states that the default is non-multiplicity of eternals unless there is a decisive proof, turning the burden of proof back on the opponent.
This is a methodological move based on the principle of avoiding multiplicity of eternal entities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : إذا جاز كون العلم باقياً ببقاء هو نفسه، فلم لا يجوز كون الذات عالماً بعلم هو نفسه، قادراً بقدرة هي نفسه إلى غير ذلك على ما هو رأي المعتزلة . قلنا : لما سبق في بحث زيادة الصفات من لزوم الفسادات ويرد على هذا الوجه أنه إذا جاز كون بقاء العلم نفسه، فلم لا يجوز أن يكون بقاء الذات نفسه، ولا تثبت صفة زائدة؟ فإن قيل : الأصل زيادة الصفة إلا لمانع ، وهو ها هنا لزوم قيام المعنى بالمعنى، ولم يوجد في بقاء الذات . لها. قلنا : خطأ ومعارضة بأن الأصل عدم تكثر القدماء إلا لقاطع . الوجه الثالث للأشعري : أن الصفات باقية ببقاء هو بقاء الذات، وجاز ذلك لعدم المغايرة بين الذات والصفات بخلاف الجوهر مع أعراضه فلذا لم يكن بقاؤه بقاء . ويرد عليه أن الصفات كما أنها ليست غير الذات فليست عينه أيضاً، وكما امتنع اتصاف الشيء بصفة قائمة بالغير فكذا بصفة قائمة بما ليس نفس ذلك الشيء. وأما الاعتراض بأنه لو كانت الصفات باقية ببقاء الذات لعدم التغاير لكانت عالمة بعلمه قادرة بقدرته إلى غير ذلك فليس بشيء لأن ذلك فرع صحة من الانصاف وقد صح كون العلم مثلاً باقياً بخلاف كونه قادراً .
If it is said: If it is possible for knowledge to be eternal by an eternity that is itself, then why is it not possible for the essence to be knowing by a knowledge that is itself, powerful by a power that is itself, and so on, according to the view of the Mu'tazila? We say: Because of what preceded in the discussion of the increase of attributes regarding the necessary corruptions. And it is objected to this point that if it is possible for the eternity of knowledge to be itself, then why is it not possible for the eternity of the essence to be itself, and no additional attribute is established? If it is said: The original principle is the increase of attributes unless there is a preventer, and here it is the necessary occurrence of a meaning subsisting in a meaning, and it is not found in the eternity of the essence? It has. We say: Error and opposition because the original principle is the non-multiplicity of the eternals except by a decisive proof. The third proof of al-Ash'ari: That the attributes are eternal by an eternity that is the eternity of the essence, and that is permissible due to the lack of distinction between the essence and attributes, unlike the substance and its accidents, so therefore its eternity was not an eternity. And it is objected to him that the attributes, just as they are not other than the essence, so they are not identical to it either, and just as it is impossible for a thing to be described by an attribute subsisting in another, so too by an attribute subsisting in what is not that same thing. As for the objection that if the attributes were eternal by the eternity of the essence due to the lack of differentiation, then they would be knowing by His knowledge, powerful by His power, etc., it is nothing, because that is conditioned upon the validity of fairness, and it has been established that knowledge, for example, is eternal, unlike its being powerful.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage presents a dialectical exchange on the nature of divine attributes. It begins with an objection from the Mu'tazila: if knowledge can be eternal by an eternity identical to itself, then why can't the essence be knowing by a knowledge that is identical to itself, etc.? The response references a previous discussion about the increase of attributes and the corruptions that follow. A further objection states: if the eternity of knowledge is itself, then why can't the essence's eternity be itself, negating the need for an additional attribute? The reply uses the principle that the default is non-multiplicity of eternals without a decisive proof. Then the third proof of al-Ash'ari is given: attributes are eternal by the eternity of the essence because there is no distinction between essence and attributes, unlike substance and accidents. The objection follows that attributes are neither identical nor distinct, and an attribute subsisting in an essence cannot be attributed to something that is not that essence. Finally, a refutation concludes that the objection about attributes being knowing by His knowledge fails because knowledge's eternity is established, whereas being powerful is not directly analogous.

Key Terms
بقاء
علم
ذات
صفات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila think that if Ash'aris accept that knowledge's eternity is itself, they must also accept that the essence is knowing by itself without an additional attribute.
Correction: The Ash'aris respond by referencing the corruptions that follow from that view, maintaining that attributes are additional despite the analogy.

Checkpoint
What is the Mu'tazila's initial objection regarding knowledge's eternity?
A) If knowledge is eternal by itself, then the essence can know without a separate attribute of knowledge.
B) If knowledge is eternal by itself, then the essence must also be eternal by itself.
C) The eternity of knowledge is impossible if it is an attribute.
D) The essence cannot be knowing because knowledge is an accident.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari position is defended by appeal to prior arguments and the principle that multiplicity of eternal entities requires decisive proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Mu'tazila argued by analogy that if knowledge can be eternal by itself, then the essence can be knowing by itself. Do you ever unconsciously compare God's attributes to human attributes, reducing His transcendence to fit your understanding? How can this passage correct that tendency and deepen your awe of Him?
?
The Ash'ari response relies on an accepted first principle: the original state is non-multiplicity of eternals. Are there areas of your faith where you hold a belief simply because it is the received tradition, without having a decisive proof or personal conviction? Will you today examine one such belief and ask whether it is truly grounded in revelation and reason?
?
This passage is a dense theological argument. If you struggle to understand it, do you dismiss it as irrelevant, or do you press in to know your Lord more deeply? What step will you take this week to better understand a difficult aspect of Islamic theology?

Ash'ari's Third Proof on the Eternity of Attributes
Presentation and refutation of Ash'ari's third proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ash'ari's third proof that attributes are eternal by the essence's eternity due to lack of distinction, and the objections and refutation that follow.

Core Idea
Attributes are eternal by the essence's eternity because there is no distinction, unlike substance and accidents.

Al-Ash'ari presents his third proof for the eternity of divine attributes: they are eternal by the very eternity of the essence since there is no distinction (maghayara) between essence and attributes. This is contrasted with the case of a substance and its accidents. However, the proof faces objections: if attributes are not distinct, they are not identical either, and an attribute subsisting in an essence cannot be attributed to what is not that essence. A final objection about knowledge being powerful is dismissed. This lesson examines this dense argument.

Guided Path
1
Summarize the third proof
Al-Ash'ari argues: because there is no distinction between essence and attributes, the attributes are eternal by the same eternity as the essence. This is unlike a substance and its accidents, which are distinct.
The proof relies on the key concept of 'lack of distinction' (adam al-mughayara).
2
Understand the first objection
The objector says: attributes are neither identical to the essence (they are not 'ayn) nor distinct (ghayr). Therefore, an attribute that subsists in an essence cannot be attributed to something that is not that essence.
This challenges the logic of attributing the essence's eternity to the attributes.
3
Analyze the second objection and response
If attributes are eternal by the essence's eternity, then they would be knowing by His knowledge, powerful by His power, etc. The response says this is invalid because knowledge's eternity is established, but being powerful is not analogous.
The objection tries to push the argument into absurdity, but the response differentiates between attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : إذا جاز كون العلم باقياً ببقاء هو نفسه، فلم لا يجوز كون الذات عالماً بعلم هو نفسه، قادراً بقدرة هي نفسه إلى غير ذلك على ما هو رأي المعتزلة . قلنا : لما سبق في بحث زيادة الصفات من لزوم الفسادات ويرد على هذا الوجه أنه إذا جاز كون بقاء العلم نفسه، فلم لا يجوز أن يكون بقاء الذات نفسه، ولا تثبت صفة زائدة؟ فإن قيل : الأصل زيادة الصفة إلا لمانع ، وهو ها هنا لزوم قيام المعنى بالمعنى، ولم يوجد في بقاء الذات . لها. قلنا : خطأ ومعارضة بأن الأصل عدم تكثر القدماء إلا لقاطع . الوجه الثالث للأشعري : أن الصفات باقية ببقاء هو بقاء الذات، وجاز ذلك لعدم المغايرة بين الذات والصفات بخلاف الجوهر مع أعراضه فلذا لم يكن بقاؤه بقاء . ويرد عليه أن الصفات كما أنها ليست غير الذات فليست عينه أيضاً، وكما امتنع اتصاف الشيء بصفة قائمة بالغير فكذا بصفة قائمة بما ليس نفس ذلك الشيء. وأما الاعتراض بأنه لو كانت الصفات باقية ببقاء الذات لعدم التغاير لكانت عالمة بعلمه قادرة بقدرته إلى غير ذلك فليس بشيء لأن ذلك فرع صحة من الانصاف وقد صح كون العلم مثلاً باقياً بخلاف كونه قادراً .
If it is said: If it is possible for knowledge to be eternal by an eternity that is itself, then why is it not possible for the essence to be knowing by a knowledge that is itself, powerful by a power that is itself, and so on, according to the view of the Mu'tazila? We say: Because of what preceded in the discussion of the increase of attributes regarding the necessary corruptions. And it is objected to this point that if it is possible for the eternity of knowledge to be itself, then why is it not possible for the eternity of the essence to be itself, and no additional attribute is established? If it is said: The original principle is the increase of attributes unless there is a preventer, and here it is the necessary occurrence of a meaning subsisting in a meaning, and it is not found in the eternity of the essence? It has. We say: Error and opposition because the original principle is the non-multiplicity of the eternals except by a decisive proof. The third proof of al-Ash'ari: That the attributes are eternal by an eternity that is the eternity of the essence, and that is permissible due to the lack of distinction between the essence and attributes, unlike the substance and its accidents, so therefore its eternity was not an eternity. And it is objected to him that the attributes, just as they are not other than the essence, so they are not identical to it either, and just as it is impossible for a thing to be described by an attribute subsisting in another, so too by an attribute subsisting in what is not that same thing. As for the objection that if the attributes were eternal by the eternity of the essence due to the lack of differentiation, then they would be knowing by His knowledge, powerful by His power, etc., it is nothing, because that is conditioned upon the validity of fairness, and it has been established that knowledge, for example, is eternal, unlike its being powerful.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage presents a dialectical exchange on the nature of divine attributes. It begins with an objection from the Mu'tazila: if knowledge can be eternal by an eternity identical to itself, then why can't the essence be knowing by a knowledge that is identical to itself, etc.? The response references a previous discussion about the increase of attributes and the corruptions that follow. A further objection states: if the eternity of knowledge is itself, then why can't the essence's eternity be itself, negating the need for an additional attribute? The reply uses the principle that the default is non-multiplicity of eternals without a decisive proof. Then the third proof of al-Ash'ari is given: attributes are eternal by the eternity of the essence because there is no distinction between essence and attributes, unlike substance and accidents. The objection follows that attributes are neither identical nor distinct, and an attribute subsisting in an essence cannot be attributed to something that is not that essence. Finally, a refutation concludes that the objection about attributes being knowing by His knowledge fails because knowledge's eternity is established, whereas being powerful is not directly analogous.

Key Terms
بقاء
صفات
ذات
مغايرة
جوهر
عرض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that Ash'ari's third proof leads to the conclusion that attributes are identical to the essence because they are eternal by the same eternity.
Correction: The objector clarifies that attributes are neither distinct nor identical; they have a unique ontological status.

Checkpoint
What is the key premise of al-Ash'ari's third proof?
A) Attributes are eternal by themselves independently of the essence.
B) There is no distinction (mughayara) between essence and attributes.
C) Attributes are accidents of the essence.
D) The essence is eternal by the attributes.

Key Takeaway
Ash'ari's third proof is defended by appealing to the lack of distinction, but it faces nuanced objections about the identity and attribution of divine attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you contemplate God's attributes, do you unconsciously treat them as separate parts of God, or do you collapse them into a single blob? This lesson shows that they are neither identical to the essence nor distinct from it. How does that precision change the way you think about God's mercy and justice in your own life? Are you willing to hold that tension, or do you want a simpler model?
?
The objection claims that if attributes are eternal by the essence's eternity, then all attributes would be interchangeable. Have you ever found yourself assuming that God's attributes are all the same kind of thing? This lesson singles out knowledge as proven eternal, but not power in the same way. What does that say about how carefully you must approach each attribute? Are you ready to study each attribute on its own terms rather than lumping them together?
?
Al-Ash'ari's proof rests on the idea that there is no distinction between essence and attributes. In your own journey of faith, do you ever treat God's essence as unknowable and His attributes as window dressing? This lesson forces you to see them as inseparable yet distinct. How does that affect your prayer life—do you praise God for His attributes as direct encounters with His essence, or as mere descriptions? Commit to reflecting on one attribute this week as truly united with His essence, not just a label.

The Divine Attribute of Takwin: Claims and Refutations
Introduces the divine attribute of takwin and presents arguments for and against its eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the debate over whether takwin (bringing into existence) is an eternal divine attribute or a temporal relational concept.

Core Idea
Takwin is not an eternal attribute but a relational meaning tied to created effects.

In this passage, the author presents the argument of some jurists that God must have an eternal attribute of creation, called takwin, and then refutes it. The refutation emphasizes that takwin is a relational concept understood from the connection of agent and effect, which is temporal, not an eternal real attribute.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to get the flow of the argument.
Notice the back-and-forth structure.
2
Identify the two main positions
Find where the jurists claim takwin is eternal and where the refutation argues it is a relational concept. Mark the key phrases.
The refutation uses 'ليس الإيجاد إلا معنى يعقل من تعلق المؤثر بالأثر'.
3
Trace the objections and responses
List each objection (praise, word Kun, perfection) and the corresponding response. Understand how each refutation counters.
The final objections are given at the end without responses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : ومنها التكوين . أثبته بعض الفقهاء تمسكاً بأنه تعالى خالق إجماعاً فلا بد من قيام صفة به يسميها إلى التخليق والترزيق والإحياء والإماتة ونحو ذلك بحسب المتعلقات وتكون أزلية كسائر الصفات. ورد بأن ذلك في الصفات الحقيقية وليس الإيجاد إلا معنى يعقل من تعلق المؤثر بالأثر وذلك فيما لا يزال . قالوا : تمدح في كلامه الأزلي بأنه الخالق البارئ المصور فلو لم يكن ذلك إلا فيما لا يزال لزم التمدح بما ليس فيه الكمال بعد النقصان قلنا كالتمدح بقوله تعالى : يسبح الله ما في السموات وما في الأرض وهو الذي في السماء إله وفي الأرض إله . وحقيقته أنه في الأزل بحيث يحصل له ذلك فيما لا يزال قالوا : اعترفتم بأنه يكون الأشياء في أوقاتها بكلمة أزلية هي (كن) وهو المعنى بالتكوين . قلنا : فيعود إلى صفة الكلام. قالوا : صفة كمال. فالخلو عنه نقص . قلنا : نعم . حيث أمكن وإمكانه في الأزل ممنوع وعورضت الوجوه بأنه لا يعقل من التكوين إلا الإحداث والإخراج من العدم إلى الوجود كما فسرتموه . وهو من الإضافات الفعلية لا الصفات الحقيقية. كما مر . وبأنه لو كان قديماً لزم قدم المكون ضرورة امتناع الانفكاك .
He said: Among them is takwin (bringing into existence). Some jurists affirmed it, arguing by the fact that He, exalted, is Creator by consensus, so it is necessary for an attribute to subsist in Him, which they call bringing into existence, providing sustenance, giving life, causing death, and the like, according to the objects, and it is eternal like other attributes. It was refuted that that is in the real attributes, and bringing into existence is nothing but a meaning understood from the relation of the effect to the agent, and that is in what is not yet [temporal]. They said: He praised Himself in His eternal speech as 'the Creator, the Maker, the Fashioner,' so if that were only in what is not yet, it would necessitate praise for that which is not perfection after deficiency. We said: Like the praise in His saying, 'All that is in the heavens and the earth glorifies Allah, and He is the God in the heaven and the God in the earth.' The reality is that in eternity He was such that this would occur for Him in what is not yet. They said: You admitted that He brings things into existence at their times by an eternal word which is 'Be,' and that is the meaning of takwin. We said: That returns to the attribute of speech. They said: It is an attribute of perfection; absence from it is deficiency. We said: Yes, where possible, but its possibility in eternity is denied. And the proofs were objected to by saying that nothing is understood from takwin except bringing into existence and bringing out from non-existence to existence as you interpreted it, and it is among the relative actions, not the real attributes, as has passed. And that if it were eternal, it would necessitate the eternal existence of the brought-into-existence, necessarily, due to the impossibility of separation.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage discusses the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence). Some jurists argue that since God is Creator by consensus, there must be an eternal attribute of creation in Him, called takwin, which applies to various acts like giving life and death. The refutation states that real attributes are eternal, but takwin is a relational concept understood from the connection of agent and effect, which occurs in time. The opponent objects that God praises Himself in the Quran as 'Creator', which would be praising future actions, implying imperfection if He were not yet Creator. The response says the praise is for the fact that in eternity He is such that He will create in the future, similar to how He is God in heaven and earth simultaneously in His eternal speech. Then the opponent argues that things come to be by the word 'Kun', which is the meaning of takwin. The response says that returns to the attribute of speech. The opponent insists it is an attribute of perfection; absence would be deficiency. The response agrees it is perfection where possible, but denies its possibility in eternity. Finally, two objections are given: first, takwin is only understood as creation from nothing, which is a relative action, not a real attribute; second, if it were eternal, the created thing would be eternal, which is impossible.

صفة
أزلية
إحداث
إخراج
إضافات فعلية

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Believing that takwin is an eternal attribute of God like knowledge or power.
Correction: Takwin is a temporal relational concept, not an eternal real attribute, as established by the refutations and objections.

Checkpoint
What is the primary refutation of the claim that takwin is an eternal attribute?
A) Takwin is a relational concept, not a real attribute.
B) Takwin is identical to the essence.
C) Takwin is an accident that ceases.
D) Takwin is a metaphorical expression.

Key Takeaway
Takwin is not an eternal attribute of God but a temporal relational concept, as shown by the refutations and objections.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage says takwin is a relational meaning tied to created effects, not an eternal attribute. When you think about God creating you, do you truly believe His act of creation is personal and temporal, or do you subconsciously treat it as a distant, static fact? How does that affect your relationship with Him today?
?
The opponents argued that praising God as Creator would be deficient if it referred only to future acts. Consider your own praise of God: is your 'Alhamdulillah' rooted in what He has done in the past, or in your present experience of His ongoing creation? Which one is more real to you right now?
?
The passage denies that takwin could be an eternal attribute, emphasizing God's transcendence. How does this shape your understanding of God's otherness? Does it humble you to realize that His creative act is not an attribute we can fully grasp, but a relation He freely chooses to enact? What does that demand of you in your worship?

The Objection on Takwin and al-Razi's Argument
Al-Sanusi presents an objection and response on the nature of takwin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that takwin is a distinct attribute bringing things into existence, and why al-Razi argues it either reduces to power or compromises divine free will.

Core Idea
Takwin cannot be distinct from power without undermining divine free will.

The debate on takwin continues with a new objection: takwin is an attribute that necessitates existence at appointed times. This lesson examines the objection, the response questioning its distinction from power, and Imam al-Razi's decisive critique.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the objection that takwin is an attribute bringing things into existence at their times, distinct from power.
The opponent claims power only makes possible, but takwin makes existent.
2
Analyze the response
The response asks why takwin is different from power conjoined with will, since power acts according to will.
3
Understand al-Razi's argument
Al-Razi presents a dilemma: if takwin effects contingently, it is not distinct from power; if necessarily, it negates divine free will.
This is a key critique of the distinct attribute view.
4
Reflect on implications
Consider why this argument matters for the Ash'ari-Maturidi debate on divine attributes.
It challenges the notion of a separate creative attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل بل صفة بها تتكون الأشياء لأوقاتها وتخرج من العدم إلى الوجود وليست القدرة مقتضاها ،الصحة، ومقتضى التكوين الوجود. على أنه لما دام وترتب عليه الأثر بعد حين لم يلزم الانفكاك ولم يكن كضرب بلا مضروب . قلنا ولما قلتم انها غير القدرة المقرونة بالإرادة؟ وهل القدرة إلا صفة تؤثر على وفق الإرادة؟ ولهذا قال الإمام الرازي: إن تلك الصفة إما أن تؤثر على سبيل الجواز فلا تتميز عن القدرة أو على سبيل الوجوب فلا يكون الواجب مختاراً وما نقل عن الشيخ أن التكوين هو المكون فقيل : معناه أن المفهوم من اطلاق الخلق هو المخلوق أو أنه إذا أثر شيء في شيء فالذي حصل في الخارج هو الأثر لا غير . ومنها : التكوين . اشتهر القول به عن الشيخ أبي منصور الماتريدي وأتباعه وهم ينسبونه إلى قدمائهم الذين كانوا قبل الشيخ أبي الحسن الأشعري حتى قالوا : إن
Then it was said: Rather, it is an attribute by which things come into existence at their times and come out from non-existence to existence, and power does not necessitate it, [but] power requires [possibility?], and the requirement of takwin is existence. Moreover, since it persisted and the effect followed after a while, there is no necessary separation, and it is not like striking without a struck object. We said: And why do you claim that it is other than power conjoined with will? Is power anything other than an attribute that effects in accordance with will? For this reason, Imam al-Razi said: That attribute either effects contingently, then it is not distinguished from power, or necessarily, then the Necessary Being would not be free in action. And what was transmitted from the Shaykh that takwin is the brought-into-existence, so it is said: Its meaning is that the concept of creating from usage is the created, or that when something effects in something, what occurs in the external is the effect alone. And among them is takwin. The doctrine became famous from Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and his followers, and they attribute it to their predecessors who were before Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, until they said: Indeed
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on takwin. The opponent proposes that takwin is an attribute that brings things into existence at their times, distinct from power, because power only makes possible, while takwin necessitates existence. The opponent argues that since the effect follows after the attribute persists, there is no separation. The response questions why it is different from power conjoined with will, since power acts according to will. Imam al-Razi's argument is cited: either this attribute effects contingently (like power, so it is not distinct) or necessarily (which negates divine free will). Then a transmission from 'the Shaykh' (likely al-Maturidi) is mentioned: takwin is the brought-into-existence, interpreted as the concept of creation being identical to the created, or that the effect alone is what occurs externally. Finally, the passage notes that the doctrine of takwin is famously associated with Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and his followers, who trace it to earlier scholars before al-Ash'ari. The text ends mid-sentence.

قدرة
إرادة
جواز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That takwin is a distinct attribute from power and will.
Correction: Al-Razi shows that it cannot be distinct without either being redundant or compromising divine free will.

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Razi, what is the consequence if the attribute of takwin effects necessarily?
A) The Necessary Being would not be free in action.
B) It would be identical to power.
C) It would be a real attribute.
D) It would be temporal.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi's dilemma shows that takwin cannot be an independent attribute without either being redundant or negating divine free choice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This passage reveals that if God were compelled to create by an attribute, He would not be truly free. In your own life, do you sometimes treat God as if He is bound by your expectations or circumstances? How would it change your relationship with Him to fully embrace His free will in every situation? Commit to surrendering one specific expectation you hold about how God should act.
?
Al-Razi's dilemma forces us to see that any attribute claimed to be separate from power either duplicates or enslaves. Are there areas in your faith where you have added necessary intermediaries between God's power and His actions (e.g., 'God must do X for me to be happy')? Identify one such belief and realign it with the truth that God's power and will are perfectly integrated.
?
The opponent wanted to safeguard God's wisdom in timing events by positing takwin. But al-Razi shows this leads to logical pitfalls. In your own life, when you try to explain why something hasn't happened yet (e.g., a prayer answered), do you ever assume that God's power is somehow limited or that He uses 'extra' attributes? Reflect on how trusting in the unity of His attributes – power and will – can bring rest to your waiting.

The Maturidi Doctrine of Takwin and its Historical Roots
Al-Sanusi reports a Maturidi view on takwin and its historical roots.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi position that takwin is identical to the brought-into-existence and its attribution to early scholars before al-Ash'ari.

Core Idea
Maturidis see takwin as the very act of bringing into existence, not a separate attribute.

This passage presents a view transmitted from al-Maturidi that takwin is the brought-into-existence itself. It also notes that the doctrine was attributed to earlier scholars. Although the text is cut off, we can grasp the Maturidi stance.

Guided Path
1
Read the transmitted view
Read that takwin is identified with the brought-into-existence (al-mukawwan).
This is a key Maturidi claim.
2
Understand the two interpretations
Two possibilities: the concept of creating is the created, or the external effect is the effect alone.
3
Note the Maturidi attribution
The doctrine is famously associated with Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and his followers, who trace it to earlier scholars before al-Ash'ari.
This shows historical roots of the view.
4
Reflect on the incomplete text
The passage cuts off mid-sentence, but the main point is clear: Maturidis hold takwin as the brought-into-existence.
The full argument may continue in the original source.

Then it was said: Rather, it is an attribute by which things come into existence at their times and come out from non-existence to existence, and power does not necessitate it, [but] power requires [possibility?], and the requirement of takwin is existence. Moreover, since it persisted and the effect followed after a while, there is no necessary separation, and it is not like striking without a struck object. We said: And why do you claim that it is other than power conjoined with will? Is power anything other than an attribute that effects in accordance with will? For this reason, Imam al-Razi said: That attribute either effects contingently, then it is not distinguished from power, or necessarily, then the Necessary Being would not be free in action. And what was transmitted from the Shaykh that takwin is the brought-into-existence, so it is said: Its meaning is that the concept of creating from usage is the created, or that when something effects in something, what occurs in the external is the effect alone. And among them is takwin. The doctrine became famous from Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and his followers, and they attribute it to their predecessors who were before Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, until they said: Indeed
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on takwin. The opponent proposes that takwin is an attribute that brings things into existence at their times, distinct from power, because power only makes possible, while takwin necessitates existence. The opponent argues that since the effect follows after the attribute persists, there is no separation. The response questions why it is different from power conjoined with will, since power acts according to will. Imam al-Razi's argument is cited: either this attribute effects contingently (like power, so it is not distinct) or necessarily (which negates divine free will). Then a transmission from 'the Shaykh' (likely al-Maturidi) is mentioned: takwin is the brought-into-existence, interpreted as the concept of creation being identical to the created, or that the effect alone is what occurs externally. Finally, the passage notes that the doctrine of takwin is famously associated with Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and his followers, who trace it to earlier scholars before al-Ash'ari. The text ends mid-sentence.

Key Terms
تكوين
مكون
ماتريدي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Maturidis add a separate attribute called takwin.
Correction: The passage shows that Maturidis identify takwin with the brought-into-existence itself, not a separate attribute.

Checkpoint
According to the transmitted view, what is takwin?
A) A distinct attribute separate from power.
B) The brought-into-existence (al-mukawwan).
C) An eternal attribute of essence.
D) The same as divine will.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi school considers takwin to be the very act of bringing into existence, not an additional attribute, and they trace this view to early scholars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
When you sin, do you see it as a defect in God's creation or as a direct result of your own choice? How does the Maturidi identification of takwin with the effect challenge you to take full responsibility for your actions?

Refuting the Objection on Boasting of Future Creation
Author refutes objection that non-eternal takwin implies false boasting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author defends divine boasting about future creation by citing Quranic precedent and the concept of eternal knowledge.

Core Idea
Describing God with future actions is valid because His knowledge is eternal.

The objector argues that if takwin (bringing into existence) is not eternal, then God would be boasting of something not yet present, implying imperfection followed by perfection. The author refutes this by pointing to Quranic verses where God describes future worshipers as already glorifying Him, showing that such descriptions are truthful based on eternal knowledge.

These verses are from Surah Al-Hadid and Surah Az-Zukhruf.
3

The Possibility Condition for Takwin as a Perfection Attribute
Author agrees but denies possibility in pre-eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why takwin, though a perfection attribute, cannot be attributed to God in pre-eternity due to its necessary relation to temporal creation.

Core Idea
A perfection attribute is only applicable where possible; pre-eternal takwin is impossible.

The objector argues that if takwin is a perfection, its absence would be a deficiency. The author agrees in principle but adds a crucial condition: possibility. This lesson examines why pre-eternal takwin is impossible, resolving the apparent objection.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objector's claim
Read the first part of the passage: 'They said: It is an attribute of perfection, so being devoid of it is deficiency.' Recognize the reasoning that a perfection must be possessed.
This is a common argument from perfection.
2
Analyze the author's response
The author agrees 'Yes, where possible' but then denies pre-eternal possibility. Think about the condition of possibility and why it is not met in pre-eternity.
Takwin necessarily relates to temporal creation; eternal possession would imply eternal creation or change.
3
Connect to divine eternity
Reflect on the theological implication: God is eternal and unchanging. Takwin, as the act of bringing creation into existence, cannot be eternally present without contradicting these attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا : صفة كمال. فالخلو عنه نقص . قلنا : نعم . حيث أمكن وإمكانه في الأزل ممنوع
They said: It is an attribute of perfection, so being devoid of it is deficiency. We said: Yes, where possible, but its possibility in pre-eternity is denied.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This is another objection-answer. The objector argues that takwin is a perfection attribute, so its absence would be a deficiency in God. The author agrees in principle (yes, where possible), but denies that it was possible for God to possess takwin in pre-eternity. Why? Because takwin is necessarily related to temporal creation, and having it eternally would entail either eternal creation or change in God, both impossible. So while takwin is a perfection, it can only be attributed to God when the effect (creation) exists, i.e., temporally.

الخلو عنه
الإمكان

Correction: The author clarifies that possibility is a condition. Pre-eternal takwin is impossible because it would entail either eternal creation or divine change, both incompatible with God's nature.

Checkpoint

A) Because God is not perfect
B) Because its possibility is denied
C) Because it leads to deficiency
D) Because it is not a real attribute

Key Takeaway
Takwin is a perfection attribute, but its attribution to God is conditioned by possibility; pre-eternal possibility is impossible due to its necessary connection to temporal creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Objection: Takwin is a Relative Action
First Ash'ari objection: takwin is a relative action, not a real attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ash'aris argued that takwin cannot be an eternal attribute because it is conceptually a relative action, not a real attribute.

Core Idea
Takwin is not a real attribute but a relative action tied to creation.

The passage presents an Ash'ari objection against the Maturidi claim that takwin (bringing into existence) is an eternal attribute. They argue that takwin is nothing more than the act of bringing out from non-existence, which is a relative action, not a real attribute like knowledge. This lesson unpacks that argument and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice how the objection is introduced and the key terms used.
The passage begins with 'وعورضت الوجوه' indicating an objection.
2
Understand the definition of takwin
The objection states that nothing is understood from takwin except 'إحداث' (bringing about) and 'إخراج' (bringing out). Reflect on why this definition makes takwin a relative action.
Relative actions (إضافات فعلية) depend on the existence of an effect.
3
Contrast with real attributes
Real attributes like knowledge do not depend on an external object in the same way. Consider why the Ash'ari consider this a problem for the Maturidi view.
This is a key point of disagreement between the two schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعورضت الوجوه بأنه لا يعقل من التكوين إلا الإحداث والإخراج من العدم إلى الوجود كما فسرتموه . وهو من الإضافات الفعلية لا الصفات الحقيقية. كما مر . وبأنه لو كان قديماً لزم قدم المكون ضرورة امتناع الانفكاك .
And the points were objected to by saying that nothing is understood from takwin except bringing about and bringing out from non-existence into existence, as you have interpreted it. And it is among the relative actions, not the real attributes, as previously mentioned. And because if it were eternal, the eternity of the created thing would necessarily follow due to the impossibility of disconnection.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage presents two Ash'ari objections against the Maturidi view of takwin as an eternal attribute. First, takwin is conceptually nothing but 'bringing out from non-existence into existence' (al-ikhraj min al-‘adam ila al-wujud), which is a relative action (idafa fi‘liyya) between agent and effect, not a real attribute like knowledge or power. Second, if takwin were eternal, then its effect (the created thing) would also be eternal, because an eternal cause without its effect is impossible—there would be a disconnection (infikak) between cause and effect, which is logically impossible. Thus, the Maturidi claim is refuted.

Key Terms
الإحداث
الإخراج
الإضافات الفعلية
الصفات الحقيقية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that takwin can be both a relation and an eternal attribute without contradiction.
Correction: The objection shows that if takwin is a relative action, it cannot be eternal because its existence depends on the temporal creation, making it temporal itself.

Checkpoint
How do the Ash'ari classify takwin in this objection?
A) As a real attribute like knowledge
B) As a relative action
C) As an eternal attribute
D) As a physical process

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari argue that takwin is conceptually a relative action, not an eternal attribute, because it is nothing but bringing out from non-existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

How does your understanding of God's creative power influence your trust in His ability to bring about change in your life? Commit to reflecting on a specific situation where you need to trust His creative power.
?
The objection reduces takwin to 'bringing out from non-existence'. When you consider your own existence from nothing, does it fill you with humility and gratitude? Or have you become so accustomed to being that you forget you were once nothing? What will you do today to remember your utter dependence on God's creative act?
?
The debate over whether takwin is a real attribute or a relative action may seem abstract, but it touches on whether God's essence is intrinsically creative. Do you live as though God's creativity is a constant, eternal reality, or do you only remember it when you see something new? Challenge yourself to see God's ongoing creation in the ordinary events of your day.

Objection: Eternal Takwin Requires Eternal Creation
Second Ash'ari objection: if takwin is eternal, creation must be eternal due to impossibility of disconnection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical problem that if takwin were eternal, then the created thing would also have to be eternal, due to the impossibility of disconnection between an eternal cause and its effect.

Core Idea
An eternal attribute cannot be disconnected from its effect.

The second Ash'ari objection builds on the first: if takwin were eternal, then the created thing (al-mukawwan) would necessarily be eternal. An eternal cause without its effect is impossible due to the principle of the impossibility of disconnection (imtina' al-infikak). This lesson explains this argument and its implications for the Maturidi claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the conditional structure: 'if it were eternal, the eternity of the created thing would necessarily follow'.
The objection uses 'لزم' (would necessarily follow).
2
Understand the principle of disconnection
The principle states that an eternal cause cannot exist without its effect, because that would imply a temporal gap or disconnection, which is impossible for an eternal cause.
This is a key logical axiom in kalam.
3
Apply to takwin
If takwin is an eternal attribute, then its effect (the created thing) must be eternal as well, which contradicts the temporal nature of creation.
This leads to the conclusion that takwin cannot be eternal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعورضت الوجوه بأنه لا يعقل من التكوين إلا الإحداث والإخراج من العدم إلى الوجود كما فسرتموه . وهو من الإضافات الفعلية لا الصفات الحقيقية. كما مر . وبأنه لو كان قديماً لزم قدم المكون ضرورة امتناع الانفكاك .
And the points were objected to by saying that nothing is understood from takwin except bringing about and bringing out from non-existence into existence, as you have interpreted it. And it is among the relative actions, not the real attributes, as previously mentioned. And because if it were eternal, the eternity of the created thing would necessarily follow due to the impossibility of disconnection.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage presents two Ash'ari objections against the Maturidi view of takwin as an eternal attribute. First, takwin is conceptually nothing but 'bringing out from non-existence into existence' (al-ikhraj min al-‘adam ila al-wujud), which is a relative action (idafa fi‘liyya) between agent and effect, not a real attribute like knowledge or power. Second, if takwin were eternal, then its effect (the created thing) would also be eternal, because an eternal cause without its effect is impossible—there would be a disconnection (infikak) between cause and effect, which is logically impossible. Thus, the Maturidi claim is refuted.

Key Terms
القدم
المكون
الانفكاك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that an eternal attribute can exist without its effect manifesting temporally.
Correction: The objection argues that an eternal cause requires an eternal effect, because disconnection (infikak) between them is impossible.

Checkpoint

A) God would be omnipotent
B) The created thing would also be eternal
C) The attribute would be real
D) Nothing follows

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari argue that if takwin were eternal, the creation would also be eternal, which is false, so takwin cannot be eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Dilemma of a Distinct Takwin Attribute
Objection and answer on takwin's effect and al-Razi's dilemma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi argument for takwin as a distinct attribute and the Ash'ari critique via Imam al-Razi's dilemma.

Core Idea
A distinct takwin attribute either duplicates power or strips God of free will.

This passage presents a key objection from the Maturidi school and the Ash'ari response. The Maturidi argues that takwin (bringing into existence) must be a separate attribute because it produces existence, while power only produces possibility. The Ash'ari counters with a dilemma from Imam al-Razi: if takwin acts permissibly, it is identical to power; if necessarily, God is not free. The passage also clarifies a statement by al-Maturidi that 'takwin is the created thing.'

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the Maturidi objection that takwin is a distinct attribute with existence as its effect. Notice how they argue that power only gives possibility (al-sihha) while takwin gives existence (al-wujud). Also note their response to the problem of temporal delay.
They claim no necessary disconnection because effect follows after a time.
2
Examine the Ash'ari response
Examine the Ash'ari counter-question and al-Razi's dilemma. The Ash'ari asks how takwin differs from power coupled with will. Then al-Razi presents a dilemma: if takwin effects permissibly, it is indistinguishable from power; if necessarily, God would not be free.
This dilemma is a powerful critique against a distinct attribute.
3
Understand the clarification
Understand the comment on al-Maturidi's statement that takwin is the created thing. The author clarifies that this means either the concept of creation refers to the created entity, or that when an agent acts, only the effect exists externally, not a separate attribute.
This further undermines the Maturidi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل بل صفة بها تتكون الأشياء لأوقاتها وتخرج من العدم إلى الوجود وليست القدرة مقتضاها الصحة، ومقتضى التكوين الوجود. على أنه لما دام وترتب عليه الأثر بعد حين لم يلزم الانفكاك ولم يكن كضرب بلا مضروب . قلنا ولما قلتم انها غير القدرة المقرونة بالإرادة؟ وهل القدرة إلا صفة تؤثر على وفق الإرادة؟ ولهذا قال الإمام الرازي: إن تلك الصفة إما أن تؤثر على سبيل الجواز فلا تتميز عن القدرة أو على سبيل الوجوب فلا يكون الواجب مختاراً وما نقل عن الشيخ أن التكوين هو المكون فقيل : معناه أن المفهوم من اطلاق الخلق هو المخلوق أو أنه إذا أثر شيء في شيء فالذي حصل في الخارج هو الأثر لا غير .
If it is said: Rather, it is an attribute by which things come into being at their times and come out from non-existence into existence, and power only necessitates possibility, while takwin necessitates existence. Moreover, since it continues and the effect follows after a time, disconnection is not necessary, and it is not like striking without a struck object. We said: So why do you say that it is different from power coupled with will? And is power anything other than an attribute that effects in accordance with will? For this reason, Imam al-Razi said: That attribute either effects in the manner of permissibility, in which case it is not distinguished from power, or in the manner of necessity, in which case the Necessary Being would not be free. And what is reported from the Shaykh (Maturidi) that takwin is the same as the created thing, it is said: its meaning is that what is understood from the term 'creation' is the created thing, or that if a thing affects another thing, what occurs in the external world is the effect itself, nothing else.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This is a longer objection-answer pair. The Maturidi objector argues that takwin is a distinct attribute because its effect is existence, while power only gives possibility. Also, since the effect follows after a time, no necessary disconnection occurs. The Ash'ari author responds by questioning how takwin differs from power coupled with will, as power also effects in accordance with will. He then quotes Imam al-Razi's dilemma: if takwin effects permissibly (it can create or not create), it is indistinguishable from power; if it effects necessarily (it must create whenever it exists), then God would not be free (mukhtar) – a problem for divine volition. The author also addresses a report from al-Maturidi that takwin is the created thing, clarifying that either it means the concept of creation is the created entity, or that when an agent acts, the only extra-mental reality is the effect, not a separate attribute. This further undermines the Maturidi position.

Key Terms
القدرة
الإرادة
الجواز
الوجوب
المختار
التكوين هو المكون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think takwin is needed to explain creation, but the dilemma shows it either duplicates power or violates divine freedom.
Correction: The Ash'ari response demonstrates that a distinct takwin attribute leads to theological problems, so it is unnecessary.

Checkpoint
What dilemma does Imam al-Razi present regarding a distinct attribute of takwin?
A) It either necessitates the created thing or is identical to power
B) It either effects permissibly or necessarily
C) It either is created or eternal
D) It either is known or unknown

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari response shows that postulating a distinct takwin attribute creates theological problems: either it duplicates power or compromises divine free will.

In your daily life, do you truly believe that God is absolutely free in His actions—including in His response to your prayers? ?

The Maturidi Doctrine of Takwin as an Eternal Attribute
Maturidi view on takwin: eternal, distinct from power, supported by early authorities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi claim that takwin is an eternal attribute distinct from power, and how they support it with early authority.

Core Idea
Takwin: the eternal act of bringing into existence, inseparable from Allah.

In this passage, the commentator introduces the Maturidi school's distinctive position on the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence). Unlike the Ash'aris, the Maturidis consider takwin an eternal attribute distinct from power. They trace this view to early authorities like Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi, whose statement about lordship without a lord and creatorness without a created thing is interpreted as evidence for this attribute. The passage sets the stage for further elaboration on the proofs for takwin's eternity and its distinction from power.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Maturidi claim about takwin
Read the passage and identify the two main points: that takwin is an eternal attribute, and that it is distinct from power.
The passage states that they 'elaborated on proving its eternity and its difference from power.'
2
Examine the evidence from early authority
Notice that they cite Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi's statement and interpret it as affirming takwin. Consider what this statement implies about Allah's attributes even without creation.
The statement 'He has lordship without a lord, and creatorness without a created thing' suggests that the attributes exist eternally even when their objects do not.
3
Define takwin as specified
The passage defines takwin as 'bringing the non-existent out of non-existence into existence. This is the core meaning of the attribute.
This definition links takwin to the act of creation, not just potential.
